Zhenjiang to Complete the Zhencheng Road by Deadline

The Zhencheng Road project has a pressing deadline. Previously, the Construction Department instructed the Zhenjiang County Government to complete the roadbed earthwork by the end of March. Chairman Chen of the Provincial Government, concerned that the agricultural season is approaching and the opportunity to recruit labor is fleeting, specifically telegraphed County Magistrate Ye to report the progress of the project and the date of completion within three days. Simultaneously, he urged all districts to actively proceed and ensure completion by the deadline.

Yin Chuanling Accused of Dereliction of Duty

Yin Chuanling, the head of the Sixth Autonomous District under the county, has recently been accused by several villagers of Baonian Township under his jurisdiction of dereliction of duty and fraud. They filed a criminal lawsuit with the court's prosecutor's office, requesting a warrant to summon Yin to court for investigation. This was approved, and the prosecutor issued a warrant. Yesterday morning, the court convened, but only the plaintiffs appeared. Yin did not comply with the summons even by the afternoon. Only the plaintiffs were interrogated, and the court ordered their dismissal, pending another summons for Yin Chuanling to be brought in for questioning and further investigation.

Jiaxing County Has Prepared Funds to Purchase and Store Grain

The Jiaxing County Grain Storage has been allocated grain storage quotas to the various townships and public offices by the county magistrate based on acreage. However, due to poor harvests, it has been impossible to collect the quotas. The County Grain Storage Management Committee considers grain storage a crucial policy for famine preparedness and has prepared over 8,000 yuan to appoint committee members to purchase 3,000 dan of grain in Wuxi. It has also been decided to build additional granaries for grain storage. The County Government Construction Technology Officer has been commissioned to design and construct them.

Special Report

Impressions of the Economic Survey of Guangxi Province (II) by Qian Jiaxuan

Early the next morning, we went to see Mr. Li Delin. Mr. Li talked about the economic prospects of Guangxi. He seemed particularly concerned about Guangxi's import surplus. Because Guangxi has a population of 12 million, all clothing relies on supplies from outside the province. Taking foreign cloth as an example, assuming each person wears one set of clothes per year, averaging two yuan, the outflow would be 20 million. "We would also like to use high tax rates to restrict the import of foreign goods," Mr. Li said, "but on the one hand, it easily causes misunderstandings with neighboring provinces, and on the other hand, it provokes opposition from merchants and the public, so there is no good solution." Mr. Li's words are worthy of our attention, because the huge import surplus is not only a serious problem for Guangxi, but also a serious problem for all of China. However, in our view, it seems that compensating for the import surplus cannot be solved solely by relying on protective tariffs. Because even if we build very high tariff barriers, foreigners can still rely on the protection of unequal treaties to open factories and manufacture goods in China. Moreover, if we do not have substitutes ourselves, high tariffs will ultimately be borne by consumers.

After leaving Mr. Li's residence, we returned to the hotel. Soon, Mr. Li Li entrusted a friend from the YMCA, Mr. Liu, to see us. Mr. Liu is an executive in the children's department of the Hong Kong YMCA and has reportedly lived in Hong Kong for over ten years. First, we hired a Taxi (street car) to tour the city for a week. Hong Kong's commercial vehicles are all parked in the center of the road or in prosperous market areas. You don't have to go to a car dealership to call one; you can hire them anywhere. But the fares are very high, starting at forty cents, about one Hong Kong dollar every ten minutes or so. There is an automatic pointer on the car that automatically points to the fare based on the length of time. We sat for less than half an hour, and the pointer had already pointed to two dollars and fifty cents. This was really too expensive, so we got off midway and took a public bus to tour the Peak Tram. The Peak Tram is a major transportation facility between Hong Kong Island and the mountain, and is also known as one of Hong Kong's famous attractions. The road was reportedly suggested and built by an Englishman, A. Finlay Smith. Construction began in 1885 and was completed in 1888. It officially opened to traffic in May of that year. In 1905, the Peak Tramway Co. Ltd. was established. Initially, the round trip took nine minutes and there were no stops. Now, although it is on the same route, it stops at six stations along the way: Garden Road, Kennedy Road, Bowen Road, May Road, Barker Road, and Peak Road, and it only takes seven and a half minutes. Also, when the car was first put into use, the body was made of wood and felt quite heavy. Later, steel cars were used. Since 1927, specially made new vehicles have been used, each of which can carry 53 passengers. On average, about 3,000 tourists visit every day. Six years ago, the car was still powered by steam, but now it is powered by electricity. The entire car is raised and lowered using a steel cable about 5,000 feet long, hence the name cable car. Since its opening, there has never been an accident. The cable car is divided into first and second class. The first-class fare for one trip up or down is thirty cents per person. After we got on the car, we sat in the first-class car. Who knew that at this time, the guide Mr. Liu secretly pulled our sleeves and said in a low voice: That i for foiregners only (that is, only for foreigners to ride). We felt very strange when we heard it. Why don't Chinese people even have the qualifications to ride first-class trams! So my companion Mr. Han replied to him very humorously, Yes, we are just foreigner (we are foreigners!). Regardless of the consequences, he sat down in first class. The fact immediately proved that first and second class were not divided between Chinese and foreigners. This was just Mr. Liu's misunderstanding. Mr. Liu himself was also embarrassed because it turned out that it was also his first time riding. The summit of the mountain is 1,500 meters above the ground. Overlooking the entire island, everything is in sight. We lingered on the summit for about ten minutes, and then took the cable car down the mountain and returned to the hotel, preparing to take the Hong Kong-Guangdong night ferry to Guangzhou tonight.

Hong Kong is 89 miles from Guangzhou by sea, and the voyage takes about eight hours. We boarded the ship at 9 pm, and the ship sailed at 12 o'clock. When the night ferry left Hong Kong, we looked out over the entire island on the deck and saw the electric torches shining brightly, like a sparkling crystal mountain. It was really beautiful. We got tired of watching the night view of Hong Kong Island, went back to the boat and slept. When we woke up, we had already arrived in Guangzhou. This voyage can be said to be the most enjoyable one in our life, because the dryness and boredom of the journey were completely replaced by a dream in the black sweet land. But there is one thing to remember on the Hong Kong-Guangdong wheel. Our cabin mate was a Cantonese man, Mr. Wang, who was studying at some school in Hong Kong. This Mr. Wang always said Sure or Of Course in every two sentences. After we exchanged names with him, Mr. Han asked him if he was a member of the YMCA. His answer was Sure why not! We were really taken aback when we heard this affirmative reply. Only later did we realize that it was an exception not to join the YMCA when studying in Hong Kong. The next day, when the boat approached the Guangzhou pier, many coolies carrying luggage saw that we were foreigners, so they tried to fleece us. Because Mr. Wang was Cantonese, we asked him if the compensation demanded by the coolies was too high, hoping that he could bargain for us. Who knew that this Mr. Wang simply replied, Sure, too much, and left on his own. We had to use half-gestures to hand over the luggage to the porters and transport it to the New Asia Hotel. Speaking of the New Asia Hotel, it is really worthy of our special praise, because most of the hotels in big Chinese cities hide dirt and accept filth, and are places where smoking, gambling, and prostitution gather. These improper businesses often form the bulk of their income. Even if the official authorities want to prohibit them, they are too deeply rooted to change, and they only do lip service. But the New Asia Hotel in Guangzhou is really an exception. It absolutely prohibits smoking, gambling, and calling prostitutes. They have posted such notices everywhere. Anyone with the above three hobbies is requested not to patronize. This clean air is something that we cannot breathe in any hotel in China. As for the elegance of the rooms and the thoughtfulness of the hospitality, those are just minor matters. So here we are willing to post a free advertisement for them. If you are a newcomer to Guangzhou, staying at the New Asia is really the most suitable.

After arriving in Guangzhou, we went to visit Mr. Zhang Renmin, Li Zongren's chief of staff. Mr. Zhang asked us to stay in Guangzhou for a few days. He said that the Fourth Army Headquarters had recently invited a German doctor, Dr. Schneider. They ordered an adjutant to send us and the German doctor to Nanning together. We didn't want to delay in Guangzhou too much, but on the one hand, there were many language barriers to go to Guangxi, and the route was too unfamiliar. At the same time, Mr. Lei Binnan also advised us to wait for the adjutant to travel together, which would be more convenient. So we had to stay in Guangzhou temporarily. During these two days, we took the opportunity to visit several friends in Guangzhou: Mr. Zhang Qiaomen (Director of the Statistics Section of the Guangdong Provincial Government) and Mr. Chen Dacai (Director of the Guangdong Investigation and Statistics Bureau), and asked them for several Guangdong economic survey forms for reference in Guangxi.

On July 20, Qiu Jiancheng, the adjutant sent by the Fourth Army to send us, came to the New Asia Hotel to inform us that it had been decided to leave Guangzhou for Wuzhou at 10 am the next morning, and told us to prepare our luggage. At nine o'clock the next day, Adjutant Qiu came. We first moved to the "Foreign Boat" (Guangdong people)

The appellation Motor Boat) crossed the Guangsan Road Station on the opposite bank, and from there took a train to Sanshui, and then from Sanshui took the Hong Kong-Wuzhou express boat to Wuzhou. The train departed at 11:10 am and arrived at the Sanshui River Estuary at 2 pm. As soon as we got off the train, we saw a large group of barefoot women in rough clothes, shouting and shouting, surrounding us and snatching our luggage. Fortunately, we were escorted by someone and were not besieged. They told me that these were all boat women who came to solicit business. Later, what we saw traveling in the interior of Guangxi was that not only was the work of rowing boats done by women, but even the dock coolies were almost entirely women, and men were rarely seen. We became accustomed to it and were not surprised. We have discussed with several friends the reasons why female labor is particularly developed in Guangdong and Guangxi. The general historical origin is that the sons of Guangdong and Guangxi participated in many wars in China in the past, and many strong men died in the gullies, so women naturally had to participate in production labor. On the other hand, the custom of men in Guangdong and Guangxi to take concubines is particularly prevalent. Their so-called "concubines" are by no means the so-called "aunties" in Shanghai who are pampered and privileged, but at the same time they are also purchases of cheap labor. This is a disguised form of female labor. Sometimes a man's labor often cannot maintain the life of a family, so his wife and daughter have to do some odd jobs to supplement the family. For example, the incense workers in Liuzhou have an average of three months of unemployment every year. At this time, they rely entirely on their wives to fetch water to maintain their lives. This is probably an economic basis for the continued development of female labor.

After arriving in Sanshui, we transferred to the Hong Kong-Wuzhou express boat. The boat departed at 5 pm and arrived in Wuzhou at 9 am the next morning. This was truly entering Guangxi. Wuzhou has always been known as "the Shanghai of Guangxi." In fact, Wuzhou's importance to Guangxi is even greater than Shanghai's importance to China. It is not only the passage from Guangxi to Guangdong, but also the center of foreign trade for the three provinces of Guangxi, Yunnan, and Guizhou. Geographically and militarily, Wuzhou controls the throat of the West and Two Rivers. Economically, it is a gathering area for commerce, industry, and finance in Guangxi Province. The city of Wuzhou was established before, but the municipal government was abolished in the 20th year of the Republic of China and returned to county rule. However, the current Municipal Public Security Bureau and Municipal Works Bureau are still directly under the Nanning Provincial Government. Regarding Wuzhou, we will have a more detailed description later.

Local News

Bank Association Cables Roosevelt's Original Text

Since US President Roosevelt implemented a monetary policy to lower the price of the US dollar in order to raise the price of silver, China, as a silver-using country, faces the crisis of silver gradually flowing out of the country. On the 20th, the Bank Association urgently cabled Roosevelt, asking him to pay attention. The association believes that this matter involves international negotiations, and the content of the telegram is strictly kept secret. A reporter from Shenshi News Agency learned the original English draft of the telegram from a certain aspect of the banking community yesterday. The following is a brief translation:

Telegram to Roosevelt Original Text

The original text roughly stated: The colleagues of the banking industry in this city respectfully express their greetings to your Excellency, the President. Since your Excellency implemented the recovery plan, the price of the US dollar has fallen, and the prices in your country have indeed risen, and the number of unemployed has gradually decreased. However, the prices of our country's products will continue to fall, and silver will inevitably flow out, creating opportunities for speculators. Moreover, our country has suffered from natural disasters and man-made disasters for thousands of years, and the people's lives have fallen into deep water and hot fire. If your country's silver purchase policy continues, our country's farmers will feel even more distressed, and international exchange rates will also be extremely chaotic. Both sides' economies will suffer adversely. Our country's banking industry colleagues sincerely hope that your Excellency, the President, will observe our country's situation and take prudent steps on the price of silver, so as not to suddenly rise and cause difficulties in exchange rates. We hereby send this telegram and respectfully ask for your consideration. Shanghai Bank Association, number.

No Reply Expected

The Bank Association's telegram was sent out on the evening of the 20th. As of last night, Roosevelt had not replied to Shanghai. According to a certain important person in the banking community yesterday, they received a private telegram from the US, which roughly stated that President Luo had not made any statement on the Bank Association's telegram. What the outcome is, it is difficult to understand. It is expected that there will be no reply to this matter, because the telegram was not sent through diplomatic channels, and President Roosevelt has no obligation to reply. However, President Luo will at least pay close attention to the interests of our country based on this telegram.

Sun Ke's Talk Yesterday

The United States Will Inevitably Raise the Price of Silver

The First Draft of the Constitution Will Be Published on March 1

Sun Ke, the President of the Legislative Yuan, left Beijing the night before and went to Wuxi for sightseeing. He arrived in Shanghai the night before. Yesterday morning, Mr. Sun met with reporters from various newspapers at his residence and gave a talk. The following is a record of what Mr. Sun said:

Different Positions of China and the United States

Sun Ke believes that the United States' raising of the price of silver is due to the different positions of China and the United States. Our country has no so-called countermeasures, because the initiator of this matter is not us but the United States. The United States regards silver as currency, and raising the price of silver is raising the price of its own country's goods to lower the price of gold. The United States is a gold-using country, and lowering the price of gold is raising the price of goods. This is very obvious. As for why the United States suddenly wants to raise the price of silver, it is because it is being lobbied by silver miners to seek benefits for themselves. The reason they hold is that raising the price of silver and lowering the price of gold can boost China's purchasing power and absorb a large amount of American goods. Who knows that this one-sided reason is completely wrong. Because China uses silver as its standard, the price of silver increases, the price of currency also rises, and the price of local products falls. At this time of commercial downturn, raising the price of silver suddenly will have an even greater impact. China is in this situation, and it is doubtful whether it can increase its purchasing power. Therefore, this move by the United States is completely a mistake in economic ideals.

Memorial Service for King of Belgium Today

Held at 11:30 am

Mayor Wu and Others Will Participate in Person

King Albert I of Belgium suffered an unfortunate death, which shocked the world. The memorial service for the King of Belgium in this city is scheduled to be held at 11:30 am today in St. Joseph's Church on Tianzhutang Street. The ceremony will be a Requiem Mass of the Catholic Church, presided over by the Belgian Ambassador Ji Youmu, with Father and Bishop Hui as the main celebrants. Ambassadors and consuls from various countries stationed in Shanghai and military attachés of the army and navy will all participate uniformly at that time. Mayor Wu of this city, Security Director Yang Hu, Foreign Affairs Director Yu Ming, Chief of Staff of the Garrison Command, and senior naval officers will not only send wreaths, but will also participate on time. The Belgian Ambassador will go to Beijing in the evening after the memorial service in this city to preside over the memorial service for the King of Belgium to be held in Beijing on the 28th.

Must Be Realized and Cannot Be Remedied

It is heard that this movement in the United States is unlikely to be changed when it is realized. There has been considerable progress, and the plan is to raise the price of silver to the ratio of gold to silver becoming one to twelve. The desire is extravagant. The current price ratio of gold to silver in the United States is one to more than thirty. Now, if they want to raise the price by such a large amount, even if the banks in this port have cabled the United States to stop it, it may be difficult to achieve results. Because the United States is quite determined to raise the price of silver, if the price of silver is raised in the future, China's silver will flow out, and hard currency will inevitably be scarce. If it is said that the export of silver is prohibited, I am afraid that it will not be effective, because China's national defense is not strict and there is no way to prevent it.

Little Impact on International Relations

As for the relationship between raising the price of silver and the international community, because all countries are gold-using countries, there is little impact. Raising the price of silver is equivalent to raising the price of goods, so the interests of gold-using countries and silver-using countries are completely opposite. The United States is a national economic country and will not take into account the interests of others, so there is nothing to do. The London Silver Price Agreement's slow approval is also useless. The National Economic Conference has not yet heard of any discussion on this matter. However, the economic experts of the National Economic Conference should study this issue. The government, in addition to the bankers in Shanghai have expressed their views, there is no other remedy. I am afraid that this move by the banking community may not be able to change the United States' intention.

First Draft of the Constitution to be Published on Schedule

Later, it was said that the first draft of the Constitution has been completed and will be published on March 1 (Thursday). After publication, it is hoped that the people of the country can study and criticize it, so that the Legislative Yuan's plenary meeting can revise and improve it, complete the second draft, and submit it to the Central Political Conference for submission to the National Assembly in April next year for approval. There are three points in this first draft that are worthy of study and are more noteworthy: (1) In the central organization, such as during the adjournment of the National Assembly, a National Committee is established to inherit its duties. For example, when the Control Yuan has impeachments of the President and other important cases, it can be requested that the Committee take over and temporarily convene the National Assembly to resolve it. In peacetime, it is equivalent to the position of a elder, prepared for government consultation. Its nature is similar to that of the Japanese elder, but Japan is not within the provisions of the Constitution, and a part of it represents the National Assembly; (2) Regarding local organizations, provinces are not called local but purely central administrative regions, and cities and counties are called local, that is, they are stipulated as units of local autonomy. In the future, when the National Assembly elects representatives, the units stipulated above will be used, and each unit will elect a representative. However, cities that are close to the capital will have other methods; (3) Educational funding has always been only one thousand several million yuan. This time, after a long discussion, either a general provision or a clear provision was made. As a result, everyone believed that a clear provision was more appropriate. Therefore, the first draft stipulates that the educational funding budget accounts for 15% of the central general budget and 30% of the local general budget. Taking the central funding of 800 million as an example, the annual educational funding can account for about 160 million yuan. Compared with the past, it is a ratio of tens to one. If this is stipulated, educational funding will never be a problem in the future, and with sufficient funding, promoting education can also reduce difficulties.

New Province Problems Rectify Officialdom

As for the Xinjiang issue, in fact, the central government does need to send senior officials to go there. However, the reason for the Xinjiang unrest is mistakenly believed to be a religious issue, which is inaccurate. Its biggest reason is due to poor officialdom, harsh government, and miscellaneous taxes, which aroused resentment, led to desperate measures, and resistance to the government. Coupled with the constant disturbances of Ma Zhongying and others, it became even worse. Most of the people in the province are Hui, and the officials are all Han Chinese. After the instigation of those behind the scenes, it is believed to be a religious issue. Therefore, the current method of pacification should first rectify the officialdom and relieve their suffering, then the root cause will be eliminated and the situation will not expand.

Absolutely No Such Thing as Electing a Premier

When the reporter asked Mr. Sun about the record of the central government's election of a premier as published in the Great American Evening News, he said that this matter was not accurate. This is stipulated in the party constitution, and if there is any change, it will be a matter of revising the general chapter. It seems that there will be no such proposal at this time, so I have never heard of it.

Kong and Song Met Yesterday Morning

Exchanged Views on the Silver Agreement

Summoned Banking Community for Talks Today

Dagon News Agency reported that Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi believes that the US government will recoin silver coins and raise the price of silver, which will have a great impact on the interests of our country. In addition to carefully considering the Shanghai Bank Association's request to postpone the approval of the silver agreement, the silver agreement was signed by former Minister of Finance Song Ziwen when he represented our country at the London Economic Conference. How should this matter be handled? It is necessary to discuss it in detail with former Minister of Finance Song. Yesterday morning, Minister of Finance Kong drove from his residence on West Innes Road to Qi Qi Road to meet with Mr. Song and exchange views on all aspects of the silver agreement. The meeting ended at 11:20 am. What the result is, it is still difficult to find out for a while. In order to carefully handle the silver agreement issue, Minister of Finance Kong has decided to summon important figures in the banking community for talks separately from today (26th) to solicit opinions for in-depth study. As for the leaders of the banking community, Li Fuxun, Zhang Gongquan, Xu Jiyun, etc., have decided to present the advantages and disadvantages to Minister of Finance Kong and continue to protest the increase in the price of silver.

American Cotton and Wheat Continue to be Shipped to Shanghai

American loan cotton and wheat have recently been shipped to Shanghai. This reporter wanted to understand the modification of the cotton contract, so he went to various parties to inquire. The news obtained is described as follows:

Contract Modification Issues

The total amount of cotton purchased by our country from the United States with loans is 400,000 tons, totaling 800,000 bales, worth 40 million US dollars. The contract deadline is the end of June this year, and all must be purchased. Since the opening of shipment, the price of cotton has been inconsistent, such as selling it at a loss, so the number of shipments to China is very small, not even one-fifteenth. The contract period is only four months, and it will be difficult to sell all of it by then. Therefore, our country has asked the US government to modify the contract. According to the reporter's investigation from various aspects, the points for requesting modification are: first, extend the contract period; second, it is difficult to purchase and transport all of the cotton due to domestic needs and market prices. Some of the cotton will be converted into machinery needed by our country's industrial factories. It is heard that this matter is being negotiated in the United States.

Two More Batches of American Cotton Arrive

American cotton has been loaded since November last year, and it has been more than three months since then. However, only 6 million yuan worth of cotton has been shipped, and the number of cotton that has been shipped and is on the way is not large. The other day, more than 700 pieces were loaded by the Pacific Company's Belanger ship and have been unloaded at Zhanghuabang. There is also another batch, which was also loaded by the company's Brantford wheel and is expected to be imported on Monday, with more than 1,000 pieces. Both batches of American cotton were purchased by foreign merchants in Shanghai.

Wheat and Flour Continue to Arrive

The total amount of American wheat and flour is 300,000 tons. Since mid-December last year, it has been loaded from Portland. As of yesterday, a total of 14 ships had arrived in Shanghai and Nanjing. The last ship loaded by the Asia wheel is still being unloaded. Yesterday, we received a telegram that the 15th ship, Jefferson City, carried a mixture of 8,275 tons of wheat and flour, and is expected to arrive in Shanghai tomorrow. There are still the 16th to 19th ships, a total of four ships, which together carry 30,000 tons of wheat and are also on the way. It is expected that they can all arrive in Shanghai for unloading before March 5. In total, there are 19 ships of American wheat, 140,000 tons, plus flour, etc., worth 10 million yuan in national currency. By March 5, the American wheat side has already been able to transport nearly half of it, and there are still 160,000 tons of wheat and flour, all of which will be loaded by the end of June.

New British Envoy to China, Sir Miles Lampson, Arrives in Shanghai This Morning

Chinese and British Representatives Prepare to Greet Him Upon Arrival

Will Rest in Shanghai for a Week Before Proceeding to Beijing

The newly appointed British Ambassador to China, Sir Miles Lampson, along with his wife and three daughters, as well as Sir De Sausmarez, who went to Hong Kong to welcome them, will arrive in Shanghai this morning aboard the British company's "Chitral" steamer. They will disembark at the Hongkou Wharf. Those present to welcome them will include representatives of the National Government, British Chargé d'Affaires Mr. Ingram, British Consul-General in Shanghai Mr. Brenan, and British Assessor Mr. Moss. Currently, due to the mourning period for the late King Albert of Belgium, all welcoming ceremonies will be kept simple. As for public banquets, there is only one invitation from a joint committee formed by the British Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai and the China Association, aiming to allow the new envoy to meet with leaders of the British community. Since the new envoy will have many official and private matters to attend to in Nanjing and Peiping (Beijing) after his arrival, delaying the meeting would cause unnecessary delays. The envoy will stay in Shanghai for a week before proceeding to Nanjing to present his credentials. He will then travel north to Peiping around March 6th or 7th. Sir Miles Lampson and his wife will reside at the British Consulate-General, while his daughters will stay at the Cathay Hotel.

Manufacturers Plan to Promote Domestic Goods Nationwide

Organizing Introduction Centers and a Joint Office

Planning to Establish China National Products Companies Nationwide

According to the Central News Agency, in recent years, the Chinese people have been working diligently to promote domestic goods. In addition to striving to produce goods to meet the needs of all sectors, manufacturers have also formed the China National Products Production and Sales Cooperation Association, which has established introduction centers to fulfill its responsibility for promotion and introduction. Furthermore, a China National Products Company has been established in Shanghai to centrally sell general merchandise, and its business is thriving. However, due to its limited scope, it is difficult to reach the entire country. Recognizing this, manufacturers have jointly organized the China National Products Company Introduction Center Joint Office, planning to establish National Products Companies throughout the country to expand sales. They have also made special arrangements with banks to regulate finances. The organization has now been established, and directors have been appointed to be responsible for planning and implementation. Yesterday, a reporter met with Mr. Cai Shengbai, Director of the office and General Manager of the Mei Ya Silk Weaving Factory, who provided detailed information on the organization and its implementation plan. The following is a summary:

Internal Organization

According to Mr. Cai, the China National Products Company Introduction Center National Joint Office, under the guidance of the China National Products Production and Sales Cooperation Association, is jointly organized by various domestic goods factories, the China National Products Company, domestic goods introduction centers, and banks. Currently, dozens of entities have joined, including the China Chemical Industry Society and the Mei Ya Silk Weaving Factory. A founding meeting has been held, and the following directors have been elected: Chairman Fang Yexian, Managing Directors Cai Shengbai, Shi Jiu'ao, Fang Jiangge, and Ren Shigang, and Directors Zhang Gongquan, Ye Youcai, Xie Bingru, and Pan Yangyao, who will be responsible for planning. In addition to the Director, the internal organization includes four sections: Finance, Management, Procurement, and Audit. The expenses are covered by tiered contributions from each member, with Class A paying 60 yuan per month, Class B 40 yuan, Class C 20 yuan, and Class D 10 yuan. If there is a shortfall, the members will contribute proportionally according to their class. Furthermore, local China National Products Company introduction centers should contribute 5% of their profits as a fund for the office, in addition to membership fees.

Business Regulations

The business regulations of the office are as follows: (1) Planning and establishing China National Products Companies and domestic goods introduction centers in various locations; (2) Jointly organizing factories as members and signing agreements to supply goods to China National Products Companies and domestic goods introduction centers in various locations; (3) Making special arrangements with banks to regulate the finances of both production and sales; (4) Auditing and supervising the business of China National Products Companies and domestic goods introduction centers in various locations; (5) Acting as an agent for China National Products Companies and domestic goods introduction centers in various locations to purchase various domestic goods and local products. If commercial leaders in various locations wish to organize their own National Products Companies, they can consult with the office in advance for approval and then raise their stipulated capital. At least one-third of the capital must be in cash for circulation. All goods can be supplied by the office and paid for after they are sold. Goods from non-member factories can also be entrusted to the office for purchase. However, a deputy manager will be dispatched by the office to supervise the business, and there will be a designated bank to advance funds. Therefore, with one share of capital, it is possible to conduct ten shares of business. Merchants can conduct the maximum amount of business with the minimum amount of capital, and the products of each factory can expand their sales. This is truly a move with multiple benefits.

Organizational Outline

Mr. Cai then presented the organizational outline for China National Products Companies in various locations and the procedures for consulting on establishing National Products Companies. The original text is as follows: (1) With the permission of the Shanghai China National Products Company, any organization that establishes a company in accordance with this outline in various locations may be allowed to use the name of the China National Products Company, but must be prefixed with the name of the location to indicate differentiation, and must also register with the competent authorities in accordance with the provisions of the Company Law to clarify responsibilities; (2) Those using the name of the China National Products Company shall limit their business to retail, while those also using the name of the China National Products Introduction Center may also engage in wholesale; (3) When commercial leaders in various locations organize local China National Products Companies, they must first register with this office. The capital shall be raised by local people; (4) The equipment costs of China National Products Companies in various locations shall not exceed two-thirds of the total capital, i.e., after the equipment is completed, there must still be at least one-third of the total capital in cash; (5) The goods of China National Products Companies in various locations shall be supplied by member factories and paid for after they are sold. Goods from non-member factories shall also be entrusted to this office for purchase, but a handling fee shall be paid; (6) The goods issued by member factories to China National Products Companies in various locations shall be valued and mortgaged by a designated bank in Shanghai. The payment for goods from non-member factories can also be negotiated with the designated bank to mortgage a corresponding amount; (7) The manager of China National Products Companies in various locations shall be elected by the board of directors of the company. The deputy manager shall be appointed by this office. The accountant and cashier shall be appointed by the designated bank; (8) China National Products Companies in various locations are naturally members of this office. In addition to paying membership fees, if there is a surplus, 5% of the profits shall be contributed as a fund for this office; (9) If there is a surplus in China National Products Companies in various locations, in addition to the aforementioned distribution, 15% of the profits shall be distributed to each member factory in proportion to the actual sales in the current year; (10) All purchases of China National Products Companies in various locations shall be handled and purchased through this office. If they wish to sell local products, they must also be reviewed by this office before they can be purchased, to avoid mistakenly purchasing non-domestic goods; (11) The limit on the supply of goods by member factories shall be determined by this office in conjunction with each member factory and each China National Products Company; (12) The contract between this office and China National Products Companies in various locations shall be for a trial period of three years. If the business performance is deemed satisfactory by this office, it may be continued for seven years.

Negotiation Procedures

As for the procedures for establishing China National Products Companies in various locations, they are as follows: (1) The initiators of establishing China National Products Companies in various locations shall request registration with this office; (2) This office shall issue an investigation form, a sample contract, the articles of association of this office, the organizational outline of China National Products Companies in various locations, and other documents such as these procedures; (3) After receiving the aforementioned documents, the initiators of China National Products Companies in various locations shall fill in the investigation form in detail within ten days, sign and seal it by all initiators, and submit it to this office; (4) After receiving the investigation form of China National Products Companies in various locations, this office shall submit it to the board of directors for review. If it is deemed qualified, this office shall notify it in writing, formally recognizing it as the China National Products Company in that location, set a deadline for its establishment, and issue a letter of intent to join as a member and appoint a deputy manager of the China National Products Company in that location (the deputy manager's allowance shall be calculated from the date on which this office formally recognizes the company as a member and shall be borne by the company); (5) After establishing the China National Products Company in various locations in accordance with the deadline, it shall submit the record of the founding meeting and the letter of intent to join this office as a member (this letter of intent shall be signed by all the directors elected by the China National Products Company in various locations) and the articles of association of the company (all provisions in the sample contract between this office and the China National Products Company in various locations that are related to the articles of association of the company shall be clearly stipulated in the articles of association of the company) to this office for safekeeping; (6) After the China National Products Company in various locations is established in accordance with the deadline and submits the aforementioned documents, this office shall review them. If it is determined that there is no conflict with the provisions stipulated by this office, the contract shall be formally signed. This contract shall be signed by the chairman or one of the managing directors of this office and jointly signed by the relevant members. The China National Products Company in various locations shall be signed by all the directors.

Joint Marketing by Chinese Yarn Manufacturers

An organization for joint marketing will be formed

Last year, Chinese yarn factories were affected by the war in North China and the encroachment of Japanese yarn. The sales of yarn in the Tianjin market were sluggish, and the inventory of yarn piled up, totaling more than 100,000 bales. Although the factories once reduced working hours and tightened up in order to maintain operations, the reduction of working hours was only a temporary measure. Clearing the inventory of yarn was not a fundamental solution. Recognizing this, the Cotton Industry Control Association advocated finding ways to clear the inventory of yarn to stabilize yarn prices. At the same time, it also planned to organize a marketing organization. However, since the Cotton Industry Control Association is a government agency, it was inconvenient to handle it directly. It was decided that the major yarn factories should automatically organize a marketing company. The preparations have been underway, and it will be formally established soon. The participants include more than a dozen major manufacturers such as Wing On, Shen Xin, Pu Yi, Tong Yi, Da Feng, Min Sheng, and Long Mao. For this organization, each major yarn factory will temporarily assign one or two people to take care of and preside over it. After the inventory of yarn is allocated, each factory will be responsible for marketing it to other ports. It is understood that the purpose of this organization is to regulate market prices and facilitate yarn sales. After its establishment, it will exist permanently so that it can be contacted at any time to respond to necessary situations.

Disabled Anti-Japanese Refugees Request Relief

Petitioning the Municipal Government and Relief Association

Zhang Xueliang Sends Representatives to Donate 200 Yuan

After the September 18th Incident, our patriotic compatriots went to join the volunteer army to charge and kill the enemy, which was a surging trend. At that time, it did give the enemy a major blow. However, in addition to those who died on the battlefield, there were many others who returned disabled. Those with broken arms and twisted feet were in extremely tragic conditions. Recently, more than 30 wounded heroes, including Wang Zhenqiu, came to Shanghai to seek help from Deputy Commander Zhang (Xueliang) and Zhu Ziqiao because their lives were difficult to maintain. The details of the events are recorded separately below.

Petitioning the Municipal Government

After arriving in Shanghai, the representatives, including Wang Zhenqiu, presented a petition to Deputy Commander Zhang (Xueliang) and Zhu Ziqiao, requesting assistance. Three representatives, Wang Zhenqiu, Dai Sirong, and Huan Zhenhai, went to the city center to petition Mayor Wu for assistance at around 11:00 a.m. the day before yesterday. They were received by Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government. The representatives immediately stated their intention to request assistance. Mr. Yu comforted them and said that the municipal government was unable to provide relief. They could seek assistance from charitable organizations in the city, as the municipal government had funds to donate to various charitable organizations, and he believed that these organizations would be able to find a solution. The representatives were satisfied with the response and left.

Requesting Relief from Charitable Organizations

In the afternoon of the day before yesterday, the representatives went to the Northeastern Refugee Relief Association in Renji Hall on Yunnan Road and presented a petition for assistance. The original text reads: "To the esteemed Association, we, Sirong and others, were indignant at the September 18th Incident in our hometown, where the Japanese used force to occupy our Liaoning, realizing their ambition to gain an inch. Recalling that the rise and fall of the country is the responsibility of every citizen, we, in our grief, rose up to resist the enemy, hoping to save the country from danger. Fortunately, our compatriots have not lost their conscience and have organized resistance, repeatedly crushing the fierce flames and giving them heavy blows. Although the enemy suffered heavy losses, we ran out of ammunition and reinforcements, and were unable to support ourselves, and ultimately failed. We are deeply saddened. Although our comrades were unable to die for the country, they all returned seriously injured. We have now been clearly dismissed by the Peiping Military Branch and sent back to our hometown, but our families in our hometown have all fallen into the hands of the enemy. Where can we go? Shall we be killed by the enemy and return to the hands of the thieves? It seems that there is no such reason in human sentiment and conscience. We, more than 30 disabled comrades, cannot think of a plan. We want to beg our compatriots for help. We are ashamed that we could not die on the battlefield and dare not have extravagant hopes. We want to make a living by labor, but unfortunately, we are unable to do so due to broken arms and twisted feet. We thought that there were many factories and a large population in Shanghai, or there would be a place to stand. Therefore, we led more than 30 disabled comrades to Shanghai. However, we are unfamiliar with the place and have no means of turning around. In this situation, we are no different from refugees. We have no choice but to ask your association to grant relief. We have no home to return to and cannot survive. Compared with refugees, we are even more distressed. We hope that your association will treat us equally and rescue us from the depths of misery. This is to inform you and ask for your consideration. Representatives Wang Zhenqiu, Dai Enrong, Yuan Zhenhai, etc."

Zhang Donates Funds for Support

In the afternoon of the day before yesterday, a reporter from the New News Agency went to visit the wounded heroes' residence and was received by Dai Enrong. According to him, "We were indignant at the barbarity of the Japanese invaders, who invaded our homeland and killed our compatriots. Therefore, we joined the front line to resist the enemy. We are only ashamed that we could not die for the country and unfortunately were injured and became social waste. After we recovered from our injuries and were discharged from the hospital, the Peiping Branch of the Military Council clearly ordered us to be discharged and sent back to our hometown. However, our hometown has been occupied by the enemy, so we had no choice but to come to Shanghai to beg for help in South China. This morning, Mr. Mi Chunlin from Deputy Commander Zhang's side sent 200 yuan for living expenses. However, our original intention in seeking help was to find possible work as a substitute for livelihood. We are determined not to rely on our compatriots with our disabled bodies. Therefore, we have agreed to keep this money as capital. If our lives can be maintained or if we do not need this money, we will donate it to other refugees to show mutual assistance among compatriots."

Rural Areas on the Verge of Bankruptcy, Urgent Need to Establish Farmers' Bank

Ningbo Native Association Sends Letter to Yinxian County Government Suggesting

Ningbo merchants in Shanghai, Cai Renchu and Dong Jing'an, are concerned about the decline of rural areas and the extreme hardship of farmers in Ningbo in recent years. If relief is not sought, bankruptcy is inevitable. Furthermore, although the Yinxian County Government has discussed the establishment of a farmers' bank, it has not been implemented for a long time. Yesterday, they specially requested the Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai to propose that the government and merchants jointly organize the bank to make it easier to proceed. The association will inform the Yinxian County Government of the situation. It is heard that the county government has scheduled a meeting on March 9th to convene representatives from various relevant groups and enthusiastic gentry and merchants to discuss implementation measures. The following is an excerpt of the correspondence:

Ningbo Native Association Suggests

Respected Sir, according to the statement presented to our association by our directors Cai Renchu and Dong Jing'an, the rural areas of Ningbo have been on the verge of bankruptcy in recent years. If we do not seek relief urgently, the hidden dangers are worrying. The Yinxian County Government had previously discussed the establishment of a farmers' bank, but it has not been implemented to this day. However, this move is indeed an important plan to relieve rural areas. If the rural areas are consolidated and the finances are abundant, all industries may be able to rely on it to turn around. If the official funds are difficult to raise, the establishment of a farmers' bank can be changed to a joint venture between the government and merchants, which will be easier to proceed. If the county government believes it is feasible, Renchu and others are willing to work hard to achieve it. We plan to forward the letter to consult with you. After checking the information, the decline of rural areas in Ningbo in recent years has become an undeniable fact. It is essential to establish a farmers' bank to circulate finances. According to the previous information, we are urgently writing to County Magistrate Chen for his review, selection, and implementation to benefit the farmers. It is not a small matter. We hope you will check and reply. Sincerely, Ningbo Native Association.

Yinxian County Government Replies

Respected Sir, we have received your letter stating that your association directors Cai Renchu and Dong Jing'an intend to establish a farmers' bank in our county through a joint venture between the government and merchants. We have received it. The proposal to establish a farmers' bank in our county has been around for a long time. It began in 1929, when local gentry were invited to hold a preparatory meeting and formulate a joint venture method between the government and merchants. At that time, the issue of interest protection and official stock allocation could not be resolved, which led to delays. In 1930, a method was proposed to raise funds for the agricultural bank by levying small industry and land, but it was not approved by the provincial government. In 1931, the province issued a method to bring agricultural bank shares under the land tax, but the township and town heads refused to take responsibility, arguing that it would increase the burden on the people. After several meetings, no agreement was reached on the amount and term of the levy. Therefore, this important measure to relieve the rural economy has not yet been realized, which is deeply regrettable. The government's plan to complete this task is to operate jointly with government and merchants, which is more feasible. However, in addition to the approximately 5,000 yuan remaining from the pest control expenses, which can be allocated for borrowing, there are no other accumulated local public funds that can be allocated. Therefore, there is no way to proceed. If local gentry can all enthusiastically assist, gather more private shares, and work together to prepare, it will not be difficult to see its early success. We have already replied to Mr. Cai in a letter some time ago, expressing this intention, and scheduled a meeting at 1:00 p.m. on March 9th in this government to convene representatives from various relevant groups and enthusiastic gentry and merchants to discuss implementation measures. We have always admired your association's concern for your hometown and enthusiasm for rural affairs. We hope that you will do your best to assist in the preparation of the farmers' bank so that we can see its early success. We especially hope that your association will send representatives to participate in the meeting on March 9th. Sincerely, Yinxian County Government.

Chamber of Commerce Telegraphes Ministry of Finance to Increase Tax on Imported Rice in Fujian and Guangdong Provinces

Orders the Abolition of Tax Bureaus and Consolidation into Customs for Collection

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce recently telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the tax on imported rice re-exported from Fujian and Guangdong provinces be increased to maintain the price of domestic rice. The original text is recorded below: "To the Ministry of Finance, Nanjing: On the 23rd of this month, we received a letter from the Grain and Miscellaneous Grain Association, stating that in recent years, the rural economy of our country has been bankrupt, and the vitality of society is declining day by day. The reason is that foreign goods are dumped, causing the price of domestic goods to be miserable, and the decline in rice prices is especially fatal to the difficulties of farmers and merchants. Recognizing this, the association submitted an appeal to the authorities through your association last summer to levy import taxes on foreign rice, and we are deeply grateful for the government's approval and implementation. However, since its implementation, the effect has not been great, and the price of rice is still low. Taking the rice-deficient areas such as Guangdong and Fujian provinces as examples, the reported import tax on foreign rice is only half of that in other provinces, which has led to foreign rice still being sold well in South China, while domestic goods are still stranded in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Hunan, Anhui, and other provinces. Reading the news, Japan's rice is oversupplied and plans to dump all the rice stored in Taiwan and Korea into our country. If this is true, what can we imagine for the future? If the import tax on foreign rice in Fujian and Guangdong provinces is not made the same as that in other provinces as soon as possible, the sales of rice in South China will inevitably be encroached upon by foreign rice, and the rice in each producing area will still be in a desperate situation. The association feels the danger and dares not remain silent. We have always admired your association's leadership of Shanghai merchants and concern for the people's suffering. We respectfully ask you to describe the advantages and disadvantages and present them to the Ministries of Finance and Industry, urging them to quickly increase the import tax on foreign rice in these two provinces. This would be a blessing for farmers and merchants, and also a blessing for the country, etc. The association has arrived. Since the implementation of import taxes on foreign rice, only Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian provinces have been excluded. At that time, the intention may have been to avoid double counting because the Guangdong and Fujian provinces had already set up bureaus to collect taxes. Moreover, at that time, the tax in Fujian was intercepted due to the changes in Fujian, and there was actually no possibility of collection. As for the people's food in Guangxi Province, it can still be self-sufficient, and sometimes it can even help Guangdong Province slightly. Therefore, the exclusion of Guangxi Province was originally a related matter, and the situation was not necessary. Now that the changes in Fujian have been settled and the government orders have been unified, the foreign rice tax bureau set up in the province can be abolished and merged into the customs to collect import taxes in accordance with the regulations. As for the import of foreign rice in Guangdong Province, it is the largest in the country. According to average statistics over the past 20 years, it accounts for almost 65%. Therefore, if the tax in Guangdong Province is excluded, it will still be difficult to block the leakage of foreign rice, and there will be no way to allocate surpluses and deficits to relieve the rural areas, and the rescue of rural areas will ultimately be empty talk. If it is said that the establishment of a bureau to collect foreign rice tax in Guangdong Province is related to the provincial treasury and it is difficult to stop it temporarily, why not merge it into the customs for collection and have the customs return the current tax amount in Guangdong Province? The rice tax collected by the bureau set up in Guangdong Province is only half of the customs duty, and it is impossible to protect domestic rice and block foreign rice. The price of agricultural products has fallen to this point, and it is impossible not to make a decisive decision. We respectfully ask your department to review and approve our request, which would be in the public interest. Sincerely, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce."

Su Ning Gunboat Sailed to Wusong Yesterday for Sea and Gunnery Trials

The fifth patrol gunboat Su Ning, built by the Ministry of the Navy for the Coastal Defense Command, was commissioned last month. However, because the internal engineering was not fully completed, the Jiangnan Shipyard continued to send workers to rush the construction. It was just completed the day before yesterday. Yesterday morning at 8:00, the new ship-building officer, Mr. Zeng Guosheng, boarded the ship with personnel from the shipyard to conduct sea trials in the Sanjia Water area outside Wusongkou. The results showed that the speed was exactly the same as the originally specified 11 nautical miles per hour. It sailed back to Gaochangmiao at around 4:00 p.m. The ship is scheduled to sail to Nanjing on its maiden voyage within the next few days. The ship has a displacement of 300 tons, is 140 feet long, 20 feet wide, has a draft of 6 feet, and a speed of 11 nautical miles per hour. The captain of the ship is Mr. Zheng Choufang.

Circular Order Requiring Employees of the Two Railways to Learn National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraphy

The Transportation Office of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways issued a circular to all employees of the railway yesterday, stating in brief:

According to the Beijing-Shanghai Railway report, the National Phonetic Alphabet telegraph instructor, Shen Haoting, of the Upper North Station stated that since the National Phonetic Alphabet telegraph instruction began on January 10 in the meeting room on the second floor, more than a month has passed. All students, except for more than 30 people, including station clerks, inspectors, station inspectors, station masters, and telegraph operators, have reported. Other students, such as section inspectors, clerks, train personnel, and station masters of Maigen Road stations, have not reported. This makes it difficult to handle and progress. However, the deadline is approaching quickly, and if the deadline expires without good results, they will inevitably bear considerable responsibility. Therefore, they dare not procrastinate and report first.

It has been found that since the National Phonetic Alphabet telegraph instruction has already begun, all employees who should learn it should follow the instructions in Letter No. 4475073 and practice together to achieve completion, service academics, so that when the National Phonetic Alphabet telegraphy is implemented in the future, there will be no risk of being at a loss. The instructor's statement that it is difficult to handle and progress is true. Please instruct all absent students to go to study immediately, so as not to be unable to complete the course due to lack of adequate results when the deadline expires.

The promotion of National Phonetic Alphabet telegraphy is imperative. All stations on the two railways, and trains on each section, as well as employees in each section and share of this office whose daily work is closely related to telegraphy, should take turns to report to the supervisors and instructors for study first. This has been instructed in a circular letter on January 13. According to the previous situation, in addition to instructing each telegraph inspector to instruct each National Phonetic Alphabet telegraph instructor to investigate the whereabouts of the absent personnel, and to contact the relevant supervisors at any time, and report, it is now necessary to issue another circular letter, so that everyone should abide by it. All personnel who have not yet reported should quickly report to the relevant supervisors and instructors for study separately and on time, in order to learn and apply it as soon as possible.

Ministry of Communications Orders Private Postal Agencies to Cease Operations

Over Three Hundred Private Postal Agencies in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces

Jointly Petition the Ministry of Communications to Maintain the Status Quo

In order to unify the postal service, the Ministry of Communications ordered the postal bureaus to order private postal agencies in various places to cease operations by the end of this year. According to Yu Ranggeng of Quansheng Private Postal Agency in this city, the letters received by private postal agencies in coastal trading ports are already sent to the post office for registration and redistribution, according to the order of the post office. As for various letters in the interior, they are still directly delivered by private postal agencies due to inconvenient transportation.

Regarding the post office's order to private postal agencies to cease operations by the end of this year, the agencies have jointly petitioned the authorities to consider the people's livelihood and maintain the status quo. After all, after the closure of the agencies, a large number of footmen who rely on delivering letters will immediately face unemployment. The locations of the private postal agencies, such as Xiamen, Wenzhou, Yantai in Fujian; Yushan, Changshan, Shengxian, Xinchang, Zhuji in Zhejiang; and Changshu, Danyang, Wuxi in Jiangsu, total no less than two or three hundred.

The China Animal Protection Association is Established

Five Hundred Notables from Party and Government Circles Attend

Directors Elected, Constitution Approved, Declaration Issued

The China Animal Protection Association held its inaugural meeting at Jueyuan, Hardoon Road, at 2:00 p.m. yesterday. Over five hundred notables from Party and government circles attended. The constitution was adopted on the spot, and directors were elected, making it a grand event. The details are recorded below.

Notables in Attendance

Those who attended included Wu Tiecheng (represented by Li Dachao), Jiang Huaisu, Huang Hanzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Ye Gongchuo, Guan Jiongzhi, Zhu Ziqiao (represented by Cha Liangzhao), Kong Xiangxi, Hu Bokang, Li Jingwei, Jin Jinan, Huang Zhuocheng, Zhao Puchu, Zhu Xiechen, Shi Yuan Ying, Dubei, Xingding, and over five hundred others. Representatives of the Party and government attended to provide guidance, including Mao Yun of the Municipal Party Headquarters and Yan Wenyi of the Social Affairs Bureau.

Meeting Proceedings

After performing the customary rituals, the chairman first reported on the purpose of initiating the Animal Protection Association (the speech is recorded separately). Then Li Jingwei reported on the preparation process (omitted). Then Li Dachao, Jiang Huaisu, Mao Yun, and others delivered speeches in succession (recorded separately). Then the constitution was adopted and twenty-one directors were elected by ballot. The meeting was adjourned after a group photo.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Ye Gongchuo reported, "The China Animal Protection Association is holding its inaugural meeting today. I am very grateful to all the guests and representatives of various institutions and organizations for attending. I would also like to thank the association on behalf of the committee. Animal protection associations are common charitable organizations in countries around the world, and are not unique to China. We should treat all kinds of animals equally and not wantonly kill them. The reason why countries have organizations for animal protection is this idea. Now, the constitutions of advanced countries also have animal protection regulations. Our China has always lacked such an organization, so that various animals have lost their protection. Given the current situation in China, the work of this association will certainly not produce rapid results. It is obviously a permanent cause, and it can also be said to be a cause of changing customs. It may take thirty, fifty, or a hundred years, but we should have a very strong force to continue our work. Now we should consolidate the foundation first, and try to add more members to cultivate the sound foundation of this association."

Li Dachao's Speech

Wu Tiecheng's representative, Li Dachao, said, "Today the China Animal Protection Association is holding its inaugural meeting, and I am here to participate on behalf of Mayor Wu. Because I did not prepare a speech, I will simply say a few words. In the past, we Chinese had so-called 'freeing of life,' but this kind of freeing of life was passive and had no strength. Today's China Animal Association is an organized and powerful organization, and it cannot be compared with the so-called 'freeing of life' in the past. Today, our responsibility for attending this meeting should be to practice what we advocate. We should also persuade those who have not participated to come and participate, so that this kind of compassionate work will slowly spread from Shanghai to the whole of China."

Party Headquarters Instructions

(1) Jiang Huaisu, Secretary-General of the Shanghai Special Executive Committee, said briefly, "The starting point of the Animal Protection Association lies in 'benevolence.' The meaning of our revolution is also the word 'benevolence.' My interest in participating in this association also lies in this. However, the scope of animal protection is too broad. The Municipal Party Headquarters has had a very detailed discussion on this issue. The result is that we should protect what is beneficial to us, and conversely, what is harmful to us, such as violent beasts and rice-eating pests, should be captured and killed by everyone. I hope that this association will also follow this principle, weighing the importance of each."

(2) Mao Yun, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, said briefly, "China has an Animal Protection Association only today. The ancients said that the way to love life is inherent in everyone. Human beings and creatures are originally only different in shape, but life is the same. Therefore, an animal protection organization is very necessary."

Elected Directors

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Cables Shandong and Henan Provinces to Strictly Prohibit the Slaughter of Lambs

Protecting Animal Husbandry to Avoid Extinction of Sheep Breeds

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a cable to the provincial governments of Shandong and Henan yesterday, stating:

(Beginning of Salutation, omitted)

On the 23rd of this month, we received a letter from the local Shanghai Cattle and Sheep Raw Leather Industry Association, stating that the leather merchant He Shunqing said in a letter, "Shunqing has been engaged in the cattle and sheep leather industry for many years. When examining its production areas, the most abundant areas are Jinning, Xuzhou, Guide, Zhoukou, and other places in the Yellow River basin. Each year, these ports produce about five to six thousand dan, and now during this recent period production has decreased by one-third. The reason is due to banditry and flooding, which have appeared in layers. However, the most serious problem is the general rural ignorance and their slaughter of fetal lambs for immediate gain. If this is not stopped, the custom will become commonplace, and the number of goats will decrease daily. In one or two years, there will be a fear of extinction of sheep breeds." Shunqing, for the sake of the leather industry, specifically requested the association to forward a request to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, and to forward a letter to the chambers of commerce in the respective ports to strictly prohibit the slaughter of fetal lambs.

According to this, the law does not allow the slaughter of fetal lambs. This not only endangers the leather industry, but also greatly hurts the heaven's virtue of loving life. Now the rural people in each port are only seeking immediate benefits and disregarding long-term harm, which is not appropriate. According to the previous situation, we should send a letter to your office, requesting you to forward it to the chambers of commerce in each port, and instruct the leather industry associations to strictly prohibit the slaughter of fetal lambs, so that the rural people in each port will be vigilant.

It has been received by the association. In light of this, if the slaughter of fetal lambs is allowed to continue, the sheep breeds will soon become extinct. Not only will the leather industry have no business to operate, but also the rural sideline products will be reduced, and the slaughter tax collected by the government will also be indirectly affected. The reasons for this matter are complex, and the root cause is the collapse of the countryside. The rural farmers have to take this temporary measure for the sake of the present. It is by no means possible for the chambers of commerce in each area to strictly stop this behavior.

We propose that your government issue an order to the county governments in each county, and to cooperate with local people, to jointly plan methods to alleviate the countryside and maintain animal husbandry, so that actions can be taken on what has been said, not just a single bulletin. May the raising and breeding of livestock flourish, and may farmers and merchants both benefit.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. Respectfully,

Banning the Slaughter of Plow Cattle

Ministry of Industry, Finance, and Interior Establish a Plow Cattle Inspection Office

The Ministry of Industry has already issued a circular to all provinces and cities prohibiting the private slaughter of plow cattle. Now, according to reports from various provinces and cities, there are still cases of slaughter and transportation in various places. At this time of spring plowing, protection should be given. Therefore, it is planned to organize a plow cattle inspection office and submit it to the Executive Yuan for approval. It is heard that the ministry has already received an order from the Yuan, and on the day before yesterday (the 24th), representatives from the Ministries of Industry, Finance, and Interior held a joint meeting and decided to not only issue a joint circular to various places prohibiting slaughter and transportation, but also decided to organize a plow cattle inspection office. In the future, the inspection procedures will be determined by specialized veterinarians. If it is determined that the cattle are old, weak, or sick, they will be allowed to be slaughtered. All other cattle are strictly prohibited from being slaughtered.

A Hero Reaches the End of His Road Due to Difficult Living

Liang Tongfang Repeatedly Fought Against Japan

Suffered from Hard Living and Attempted Suicide in a Hotel

Liang Tongfang, who served as a volunteer soldier during the January 28th Incident [Shanghai Incident] and later joined the Northeast Anti-Japanese forces, is from Shangyu, Zhejiang Province, and is currently 25 years old. After the failure of the Northeast Anti-Japanese forces, he traveled to Shanghai, but because of the difficult living conditions, he relied on pulling a rickshaw to make a living. However, everything is expensive in Shanghai, and his livelihood became even more difficult. Unexpectedly, Liang suddenly became disillusioned with the world. At about 8:00 p.m. the night before last, he brought a bedding roll and a net basket and took a rickshaw to the Old Oriental Hotel at the intersection of Hankou Road and Zhejiang Road to stay. He claimed to be Wu Chengfang, a native of Zhejiang, 24 years old. The hotel clerk led him to room 113. After Liang settled his luggage, he went out again. Shortly afterwards, he returned and closed the door to go to bed at around 9:50. Until 2:00 p.m. yesterday, he had not gotten up. The waiter on the floor became suspicious and knocked on the door, but there was no response for a long time. He quickly devised a way to open the door and enter the room, where he saw Liang unconscious in bed, his face pale, and his speech blurred. The waiter reported to the clerk, who reported to the Old Zhabei Police Station. A detective was dispatched to rush Liang to Renji Hospital for treatment. The hospital doctor administered emergency treatment and induced him to vomit the poison. It was learned that he had swallowed opium. After his consciousness was slightly clear, the police repeatedly interrogated him and he finally revealed his real name as Liang Tongfang. Wu Chengfang was an alias. By 10:00 p.m., he was completely out of danger. At the same time, Liang himself requested to be discharged from the hospital. The hospital notified the police, who sent a detective to pick him up for further action.

Deeply Poisonous and Extremely Harmful

Lu Zuode has been Apprehended and Handed Over to the Law
