Athletic Association Plans to Suspend National Zonal Football Competition This Year

Letters sent to various regions have received no response

Conflicts with Far Eastern Preliminary Selection

According to the results of last year's meeting of representatives from various regions in Wuchang, the national zonal football competition for this year was originally scheduled to be held in Sichuan. However, due to the urgent anti-bandit warfare situation in Sichuan, it is difficult to hold the competition there, and there may be discussions about holding it elsewhere. Zhou Jiaqi, an executive of the All-China Athletic Federation, told reporters that the Federation has sent letters to various regions twice to solicit opinions on the location of the competition and whether to participate, but has received no response to date. The Federation also believes that the preliminary selection for participation in the Far Eastern Games will be held in Shanghai in April, and the national zonal football competition, even if held, will conflict with it. Therefore, the Federation plans not to hold this year's zonal football competition.

Chinese and British Shooting Match: Li Gongying Takes the Lead

British Butler Takes the First Impact

Begins at 5:30 PM Today

The long-awaited second Sino-British International Shooting Match will begin at 5:30 PM today at the Shanghai Amateur Shooting Association inside the United China Society at 27 Beijing Road. China's shooting king Li Gongying will take the lead, and Britain's Butler will take the first impact. The competition target is 750 points, and the match is expected to last about an hour and a half. Admission tickets are one yuan per person. As each side prepares to compete, the audience is bound to gather, and there may be overcrowding.

Past Performance

The Sino-British International Shooting Match in Shanghai began in March last year, hosted by the Shanghai Amateur Shooting Association. At that time, the Chinese team defeated the British team by a total of 834 points, winning the first championship. The Chinese representatives were Li Gongying, Shen Lince, Zhang Yingda, Liu Fuzong, and Xu Shizhang, five outstanding shooters. The British team was led by veteran Bernard, with Maxwell, Nema, Baker, and Marks as deputies. In five matches, China won four and lost one, securing the final victory.

Current Strength

The Chinese lineup remains the same as this year, but its strength is greater than in previous years. Shooting King Li Gongying has shown significant progress in his recent performance with world-class shooter Smith. Winning the enemy today is a foregone conclusion. The other veterans, such as Yan Lince, are experienced, and Liu Fuzong, Xu Shizhang, Zhang Yingda, and others have excellent skills. There is a great hope of winning the second championship together.

British Lineup

Most of the five British representatives have been changed. The absence of veteran Bernard is a great loss to the British team. New players such as Butler, Nicolls, and Greening are also among the best of their time. In terms of actual strength, there has been no significant improvement compared to last year, but if they can proceed cautiously when facing the enemy, their situation may be balanced.

New Large Sports Ground Built in the Soviet Union

Covers an area of slightly less than 300 hectares

Grandstand Capacity of 80,000 People

(Kharkov TASS News) Here, they are engaged in building the largest sports and cultural ground in Ukraine, covering an area of 280 hectares. This stadium will be used for mass sports education, sports competitions, public demonstrations, and Red Army parades. The grandstand can accommodate 80,000 people. Near this large sports ground, a large sports and cultural palace and a sports training research institute are also being built. In addition, there are special exercise grounds, swimming pools, etc., for children's use. The large swimming pool is a total of 3,500 cubic meters and can accommodate 1,500 people swimming at the same time. For the construction of this large sports stadium and its surrounding buildings and gardens, the government has allocated 50 million rubles. Part of this year's world sports competition will be held in this stadium.

Recently, the Chinese people have been advocating sports, and the academic community across the country is making tireless efforts to promote it. Football has become popular for a time, and as a result, the demand for leather balls has suddenly increased in recent years, and the number of manufacturers producing leather balls has also increased. However, foreign leather balls occupy a very large market share due to their superior quality.

Cross-country Running Practice Held Eight Times Yesterday Morning

The Jiangwan cross-country run organized by the Western Sports Club held its eighth practice yesterday at 10:30 AM. However, due to the continuous rain in recent days, the country roads were very muddy and difficult to walk on, so the route had to be changed. Starting from Hongkou Park, they went along Jiangwan Road to the Western Sports Club Road and went directly to the Jiangwan Racecourse. Education News

Central University Establishes Educational Experiment Institute Outside the City

Since Dr. Ai Wei took office as the dean of the College of Education of National Central University, he has been making tireless efforts to rectify it. In addition to hiring famous professors and enriching the Department of Education, he also suggested that the school establish an Educational Experiment Institute. It was approved at the school affairs meeting yesterday. The main purpose of establishing the institute is to solve educational problems through psychological and statistical experiments and to establish a Chinese-style scientific education. Based on his 15 years of experience in educational psychology experiments, Dr. Ai is convinced that educational problems cannot be solved solely by imitating methods. It is necessary to discover facts or truths through psychological experiments and statistical inductions. The institute will gradually conduct large-scale experiments based on this proposition. The internal organization is roughly divided into two major departments: research and exhibition. Each department has several groups. The research department has psychology and statistics groups, etc. The exhibition department has educational material collection, teaching aids, children's toys, primary and secondary school textbooks, psychological instruments, statistical charts, and other groups. The detailed organization is determined according to actual needs. It is reported that the school affairs meeting of the college has appointed Professors Ai Wei, Xiao Xiaorong, Du Zuo Zhou, and Xu Keshi as members of the preparatory committee for the Educational Experiment Institute, which will be formally established soon and will actively proceed. The institute plans to publish a special series on psychological and educational experiments in stages. The first issue is "Conditions for Determining Perceptual Units" (written by Xiao Xiaorong), and the second issue is "Chinese Character Measurement" (written by Ai Wei). The second special issue is already in printing and is scheduled to be published in early March. Professors Du Zuo Zhou, Xu Keshi, Zhang Shiyi, Zhao Yichen, Xia Zhanchu, Wu Nanxuan, Pan Shuishu, Wang Shulin, and others are also engaged in various educational experiments, and there will be more special issues to be added and published continuously in the future. If educational institutions have problems that need to be solved scientifically, the institute is very willing to accept their entrustment to conduct experiments.

Provinces and Schools Respond to the False Accusation Case of the Qixia Rural Normal School Principal

Jiangsu Provincial Yangzhou Middle School sent a telegram to the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Joint Association regarding the false accusation against Principal Huang of the Provincial Qixia Rural Normal School by the monk Jiran of Qixia Temple. (Omitted) A letter from all colleagues of the Qixia Rural Normal School stated that the monk Jiran of Qixia Temple colluded with witnesses, fabricated facts, and falsely accused Principal Huang Tongyi in the Jiangning Local Court. The judicial authorities arbitrarily sided with the accuser, resulting in the principal's defeat in the lawsuit. They hoped to receive support and attached a copy of the judgment and statement of reasons. Upon receiving this, it was found that judicial independence meant outsiders should not interfere. However, it was heard that the monk Jiran of the temple was cunning and fond of litigation, which was widely known. Over the years, his purpose had been to eliminate dissidents. Rural normal schools were the cultural centers of rural areas, and Principal Huang was the leader who worked hardest to promote culture. The school was located near the temple, and Jiran harbored sinister intentions, viewing others as he viewed himself, believing that Confucianism and Buddhism could not coexist. He harbored resentment in his heart and made repeated unsuccessful attempts. Last year, he colluded with a group of unscrupulous people to file a lawsuit, which resulted in his defeat. As a result, his resentment deepened. It was believed that the rural normal school was a nationally renowned school, and Principal Huang was an expert in implementing rural education. How could they allow him to be implicated in public affairs and cause such a great loss to the future of rural education? It was proposed that the association make a public decision to provide strong support, and at the same time, report the crux of the problem to the provincial office to protect Principal Huang, and publish the facts in the newspapers to solicit strong opinions to awaken the attention of the legal community. In addition to sending telegrams, it was requested that the facts be presented to the council for a public decision. It was heard that the school association had submitted it to the standing committee for discussion and would have a serious response. It was also heard that the faculty and staff of schools such as the Provincial Zhenjiang Normal School had also responded one after another, arousing the attention of all sectors of society and preventing those serving in provincial educational institutions from being destroyed.

Regulations on Overseas Chinese Primary and Secondary Schools Revised by the Ministry of Education (Continued)

Chapter X: Research Association

Article 44: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools should broadly establish research associations for secondary or primary education, with the principal as the chairman and all teaching staff as members.

Article 45: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools may jointly establish inter-school research associations with local schools. The members shall be the principals and teachers of each school, and they shall be divided into groups for research on "subjects," "moral education," and "school administration," etc. Each group shall meet at least twice a month, and each year, representatives from each group shall be elected to hold a meeting once. The detailed organizational rules shall be drafted by the relevant consul in conjunction with representatives from each school and submitted to the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission for record and implementation.

Article 46: The purpose of the research associations for overseas Chinese secondary education or primary education and the inter-school research associations is to study education. The focus of research shall be on "curriculum," "academic affairs," "teaching and moral education methods," and "school administration." They shall not involve issues outside of education.

Article 47: The meeting format for research associations for overseas Chinese secondary education or primary education and inter-school research associations shall all follow the "Elementary Principles of Civil Rights."

Chapter XI: Supplementary Provisions

Article 48: Overseas Chinese may, depending on the circumstances of their place of residence, establish simplified primary schools. The methods for this will be determined separately.

Article 49: These regulations shall be jointly promulgated and implemented by the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission.

The Ministry of Education has revised the regulations for the registration of overseas Chinese schools as follows:

Article 1: Whenever citizens of the Republic of China reside in other countries and establish schools in their place of residence, the founders must have their representatives prepare a registration petition and two copies of supporting documents, which shall be submitted through the relevant consul to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, which shall then jointly review and handle them with the Ministry of Education. In areas where there is no consul, when overseas Chinese schools apply for registration, they may request local or nearby overseas Chinese educational organizations to forward the application or submit it directly to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, which shall then jointly review and handle it with the Ministry of Education.

Article 2: All overseas Chinese schools must meet the following qualifications in order to apply for registration:

A. Funding: There must be definite assets, funds, or other reliable income sufficient to maintain the school's annual expenses.

B. Facilities: There must be adequate facilities.

C. Teaching Staff:

1. All teaching staff must be qualified and competent.

2. There must be at least one full-time teacher for each class.

3. The principal must be a national of the country. However, in special circumstances, if it is necessary to hire a foreigner as principal, the relevant consul or the entire school board must submit a request to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, which shall consult with the Ministry of Education for approval.

Article 3: When overseas Chinese schools apply for registration, they must provide the following information, along with a floor plan of the entire school and a description, for review:

1. School name (if there is a foreign language name, it should also be included).

2. School type.

3. School address (in Chinese and foreign languages).

4. History of establishment.

5. Source of regular expenses and a statement of regular and temporary budgets.

6. Organizational regulations and various rules.

7. Catalog of textbooks and reference books.

8. List of books, instruments, specimens, school equipment, and various facilities related to physical education and hygiene.

9. Curriculum vitae of teaching staff.

10. List of students and a list of graduates over the years.

Article 4: All aspects of the organization, curriculum, and other matters of registered overseas Chinese schools must comply with current educational laws and regulations, unless there are special circumstances and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, in consultation with the Ministry of Education, approves modifications.

Article 5: Registered overseas Chinese schools may be given preferential treatment for matters such as commendation, subsidies, and the introduction of students to return to China for further education.

Article 6: If the Ministry of Education or the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission deems that a registered overseas Chinese school is not well-managed, it may order it to improve. If it repeatedly fails to comply after being ordered to improve, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, with the consent of the Ministry of Education, may revoke its registration.

Article 7: If a registered overseas Chinese school wishes to change or close down, it must submit a request through the relevant consul to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, which shall then jointly review and handle it with the Ministry of Education. In areas where there is no consul, it may request local or nearby overseas Chinese educational organizations to forward the application or submit it directly to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, which shall then jointly review and handle it with the Ministry of Education.

Article 8: These regulations shall be jointly promulgated and implemented by the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission.

After Chen's dismissal, the Education Department ordered the Wuhu Commissioner's Office to recommend a candidate for the bureau director. Wuhu Commissioner Wang Zhuren, due to the shortage of Wuhu County education funds and the current order to implement short-term compulsory education, felt it would be more difficult and proposed to abolish the county's education bureau. He proposed adding a section to the fourth division of the Commissioner's Office to take charge of local educational administration, saving the original educational administrative expenses to carry out short-term compulsory education. Yu Guoguang, the original supervisor of the Education Bureau, was appointed as the head of the section. The Education Department replied to the office approving the proposal and ordered the amount of savings and the plan for compulsory education to be sent to the department for record.

Organizing Vaccination: The Education Department yesterday ordered all provincial People's Education Centers to promptly organize vaccinations in conjunction with local hospitals, charitable organizations, and county education bureaus on a regular basis, and to take the opportunity to promote knowledge about vaccination.

Local News

The School Rent Reduction Committee Asks the Mayor to Express His Opinion on Rent Reduction

Shanghai's Rent is the Most Expensive Among All Cities in the World

The Poverty of Citizens is Sacrificed for the Wealth of Landlords

All Schools Suffer from Rent Pressure and Find it Difficult to Maintain

The Shanghai School Rent Reduction Movement Committee wrote to Mayor Wu yesterday, saying, "Mayor Wu, we pay our respects. In recent years, Shanghai's situation has been affected by the global economic downturn externally and the collapse of the rural economy internally. Industries and businesses are on the verge of bankruptcy, and people's livelihoods are in dire straits. Your Honor has been in charge of Shanghai for two years, and we deeply admire your detailed plans for the prosperity of this great Shanghai. Now,

Society is Gradually Approaching the Brink of Ruin

Municipal facilities face many difficulties, and the prosperity of Shanghai is even more unattainable. This is a shared pain for all three million citizens of Shanghai, and we believe Your Honor shares the same feeling. Due to the decline of the social economy, the price index is gradually showing signs of decline, while housing rents have become increasingly expensive due to the monopoly of real estate operators in recent years. The majority of citizens' monthly income is used for the insatiable exploitation of landlords. The level of expensiveness is the highest among all cities in the world. Therefore, in less than a month, the rent reduction movement has gained momentum. It is not something that a few people can promote, but a social trend and a consistent demand of all citizens. Our committee has nearly a thousand schools in Shanghai that rent houses, all of which are under severe pressure from high rents. Maintaining the status quo is already difficult, let alone development and expansion. Education is a social undertaking, a century-old plan for the country, and the lifeline of the nation. The implementation of rent reduction is more urgent than for shops and organizations. Therefore, we have gathered various schools to organize groups and work together, hoping that Shanghai education will be revived and

Build a Century-Old Foundation for the Prosperity of Great Shanghai

Previously, it was reported that a committee member of the Shanghai Rent Reduction Movement Committee said that the rent reduction movement is the hope of Shanghai citizens and one of the municipal facilities. After two months, the municipal authorities have not expressed any opinion, and there is nothing to follow, so he requested to resign. Our committee would like to express our most sincere intentions and send this letter specifically, respectfully requesting you to provide guidance for us to follow. We wish you well. The Shanghai School Rent Reduction Movement Committee."

Decided on a Plan for Rejuvenating the National Spirit Training Materials

Elected Huang Renzhi, Yu Qingtang, etc. as Standing Committee Members

Understand the glorious figures of the nation since ancient times. Understand the glorious facts of the nation since ancient times. Understand the facts of recent national humiliations and national disasters. Understand the facts of recent patriotic and national salvation efforts. Understand the latest international trends. Understand the dangers of the national economic future. Understand the facts of foreign national rejuvenation. Ugly: Action Aspect: Things that should be done, things that should not be done. Mao: Suitable for other training institutions. (C) Methods: Sub: Compiled by the Society itself. Ugly: Consult with the education authorities of various provinces and cities for editing. The President of Ginling College Gives a Lecture on Impressions and Thoughts of Traveling in the United States

The Huadong Christian Education Association of this city held a members' fellowship meeting at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA last night at 7 p.m. Dr. Wu Yifang, the president of Ginling College, Nanjing, was specially invited to speak about her impressions and thoughts of traveling in the United States. More than 60 principals of various churches, guests, and others attended, making it a grand occasion. Yang Xizhen, the principal of McTyeire School, presided over the meeting and gave a speech. Then, Ms. Wu gave a speech about her personal observations, briefly saying that she attended three major conferences. The first time she participated in the World Women's Conference was after the Chicago Exposition in July last year. Although the representatives from various countries were not many, the conference was still successfully opened. She felt that the American women's movement has been making great progress in recent years, without fear of hardships. All sectors have expressed their support for women's participation in politics. On the other hand, it is impossible for Chinese women to seek economic independence in society. The difference is too great. This is a matter for the women themselves, and women must be aware of it themselves. The second time she participated in the Fifth Pacific Science Congress, also in Chicago. This is a regular meeting held every two years, and the discussion was only about the security issues of countries along the Pacific Ocean. Mr. Hu Shi has already given a detailed report on this matter. The third time was to participate in the general assembly of the Missionary Association's traveling lecture group. After more than 80 days, she visited 32 cities in 16 states. The number of listeners exceeded the previous record. The current economic downturn is not limited to a certain country or region, but has become widespread and acute. This time, she spent a short time in the United States and did not have an in-depth study of its national conditions. However, the biggest thing she saw on the surface was the problem of unemployment. Many people came from other provinces to seek work, but they did not have money to stay in hotels, so Central Park was full of people. The state of sleeping in the open air was pitiful. Therefore, there were many relief organizations to help people avoid starvation. Major middle schools and universities were also facing salary cuts, some even up to 50%, but it was still difficult to continue. The degree of economic downturn can be imagined. As for the perfection of the facilities and the seriousness of the management, we can learn from them. For example, if the principal wants to give a speech to all the students, he does not need to gather them in the auditorium. He can just talk in his office at any time. The builders of high-rise buildings often built half of them and did not have the money to continue building. Although the number of cars on the street has increased compared to previous years, most of them are old and broken. The coolness of the stores and the lack of attention to the writing rooms are deeply affected by the world trend. However, since President Roosevelt took office, his recovery plan, currency inflation, increased production, and reduced unemployment have attracted worldwide attention. In terms of unemployment alone, there were more than 18 million people unemployed in the previous year, but now it has been reduced to more than 80%.

Free Talk

Fate

— Ni Shuoer

Mr. Zonghan pointed out with emotion that the poor old woman in the movie "Sister Flowers" said to her poor daughter: "Poor people are always poor, you have to be patient!" This is called "the philosophy of the poor."

Naturally, this teaches people to be content with poverty, which is based on "fate." Many sages of ancient and modern times have advocated this theory, but there are also "always" quite a few poor people who are not content with poverty. "A wise man may still make a mistake." The "mistake" here is that a person's fate "is always" unknowable until after the coffin is closed.

There have also been people who predict fate. Fortune tellers and astrologers are everywhere. However, they are rarely willing to determine that their patrons will be poor to the end. Even if they do, everyone's theories cannot be consistent. A says they should be poor, but B says they should be rich. This makes the poor unable to believe in their fixed future fate.

If you don't believe in fate, you can't "be content." The poor buying lottery tickets is a kind of "unreasonable expectation." But this is not without benefit to the country now. However, "every advantage has its disadvantage." Since fate is unknowable, why can't the poor dream of becoming emperor? This led to the appearance of the "Tui Bei Tu" in China. According to the Song people, during the Five Dynasties, many people looked at this picture and named their sons, hoping to correspond to the auspicious signs of the future, until Emperor Taizong of Song (?) drew one hundred copies at random and circulated them with other books. Readers saw that the order was very different and could not agree on which was the correct version. Only then did people stop treasuring it. However, during the September 18th Incident, Shanghai was still selling newly printed copies of "Tui Bei Tu."

"Contentment with poverty" is indeed the key to peace in the world, but if there is no way to specify the ultimate fate, it will not be possible to make people give up completely. Modern eugenics can be said to be scientific, and some people in China are advocating it, hoping to help the theory of fate, but history just doesn't cooperate. The father of Emperor Gaozu of Han was not an emperor, and Li Bai's son was not a poet. There are also biographies that talk endlessly about who in the West succeeded through adventure and who got rich empty-handed.

It has a clear record that the theory of fate is not enough to govern the country and pacify the world. If you still want to use it as a tool, then China's fate will really be "poor" and boring.

About My Creation

— He Jiahua

A week ago, a friend told me that a Mr. Scavenger on a certain publication scolded me, saying that I was a rising star of the "Shanghai School," and all my novels were written by Mr. Xu Zhuanfeng and Mr. Chen Fuxi. In Shanghai, scolding people is not a big deal. It seems that I have been scolded several times, but I have never made any statement or intended to defend myself, but this time I can no longer remain silent.

The fact is very obvious, my style is completely different from the styles of those two. It is a recognized fact that a writer's style is closely related to his personality. My mind is very narrow, my actions are very restrained, and I like to get to the bottom of everything and analyze it in detail. I am not willing to relax even in the smallest places. This conservative, perhaps backward, temperament is clearly reflected in my work. Although it cannot be said mechanically, generally speaking, my works have the following characteristics: (1) tight layout (2) delicate description (3) very careful use of words and sentences. I love psychological descriptions and landscape descriptions the most, and I am most satisfied with these two. The works of Xu and Chen are completely opposite to me. They write more concisely. They have always neglected the points that I pay attention to. I like twists and turns, but they love straightforwardness. I like gorgeousness, but they love simplicity. This difference in style and technique can be understood by simply looking at our works and making a comparison. As for the content, we are also far apart. My material is often very trivial, very ordinary stories, with a bit of philosophical meaning, and sometimes it is completely rural, with a poetic romance, which is absolutely different from the materials they use. Moreover, most of my works are written in the first person, and I like to set off the story as warm and enthusiastic, while they consistently use the third person, cold and plain, a bit like the style of naturalism. Readers can easily distinguish this difference after reading our works.

I have always been honest in my writing, and I have never wanted to try anything that is sloppy. Although I am good friends with Xu and Chen, there is absolutely no collusion in passing articles privately. "The beauty of a wife belongs to others, the goodness of an article belongs to oneself." Who would be willing to give away their proud work to relatives and friends? I do not deny the fact that there are famous writers in Shanghai who buy articles from unknown writers, but I am not a well-connected famous writer, and they are not unknown writers who are hitting walls everywhere. How could I have bought their manuscripts? Mr. Xu has recently published his articles in various magazines, and Mr. Chen has published several collections in Guanghua Guangming. Would they worry about not having a way out?

I write articles very carefully. There are novels that I have reviewed several times, and even short essays I don't relax, carefully considering and revising each word and sentence. Although there are times when I deal with it carelessly, it is not very often. For example, the few pieces that I am more satisfied with and that have been praised by others: Cat, On the Lake, Rainy Day, Waterwheel, Prison Break, and Slipping into the Wheels Again have all been revised several times.

Mr. Scavenger wants to use his "historical brush" to clean up the literary world. His courage and acumen are admirable, but he did not present any evidence, and he did not use his real name, which inevitably makes people suspect that he is spreading rumors. This kind of rumor-mongering and slanderous behavior is probably a "Shanghai School" trick.

"Economic Independence"

— Ms. Xiyu

Before graduating from middle school, I often fantasized like this: after graduation, how to find a job to become economically independent and avoid being angry with men. Yes, I graduated. When I went into the society, all the jobs were not what we women could do; ah, it turned out that everything we learned was useless! However, in order to implement my idea of "economic independence", I still tried to "hit" as much as possible; but when I hit the east, I heard about the economic panic, and when I hit the west, I heard about the unemployment panic, not to mention that I was just a middle school graduate! Suddenly there was good news: Company X fired a dozen male employees who asked for a raise and went on strike, and recruited women to supplement them. I had been sitting at home for more than a year, so I was not willing to let go of this opportunity. Although I heard that the salary of female employees was half that of the fired male employees, I still felt very happy and satisfied!

The female colleagues who came in with me were very gentle and often smiled at me; but I looked down on them a little: they paid attention to dressing up, their faces were white, their mouths were red, their hair was permed like lion heads, and the perfume that helped the temptation of meat filled the entire office from their bodies, attracting those male colleagues to often move their noses and explore in the air. But since they were able to run out of the boudoir to be employees, they were considered more progressive women. I sometimes thought like this.

The male colleagues were certainly a little jealous of us, because not only did our entry break their request for a raise, but also their rice bowls were even more insecure in the future, because the manager could always recruit some women to replace them. But because we were "women", they were finally very happy, listened respectfully to the manager's instructions, and patiently guided us to copy this and do that.

As for the manager, he treated us very specially: next to our seats, he specially placed a warm electric stove; every afternoon, he often asked the tea room to send snacks for us to eat. His hair was particularly shiny, and he often stood by our side, guiding this and inspecting that. He took the opportunity to talk to us, or argued with us with a laugh, about what movies, how to dance, and so on. Once he even "called" us to attend his family's tea dance party, and even "took" us to see a movie.

Of course, the next day I heard the male colleagues laughing from their noses.

We were originally able to go home at 5:00 pm every day. But when the male colleagues had left the office, the female colleagues were still buried in their work. I felt too embarrassed to leave alone; but if I waited, I always waited for more than an hour or two, until everyone had figured out everything in the company before they put on their powder and went out. Therefore, the manager praised us in public. But this praise aroused even more resentment from the male colleagues.

"Rotten goods," "fox spirits," as soon as the manager turned around, these dirty names were passed from the male colleagues. I looked at the female colleagues, their faces were red, their heads were lowered, and they were silently doing their own work.

"Ah, this is called economic independence!"

When I angrily left the company, I don't know who threw a sentence behind me:

"Vase!"

Spending the New Year in Guangzhou

— Wei Li

XX:

Friend, I really didn't expect to spend the New Year in Guangzhou this year!

I remember this time last year, we happened to be living on Mount Saint-Thierry in France. On New Year's Eve, a few of us friends agreed to go to Old Shen's house to eat roast chicken, drink wine, play cards, and make noise until dawn. We were having a great time, and you said, "We don't know where we will spend the New Year next year"? "I will definitely be at home," I answered you firmly. Who knew that I would be spending the New Year in a foreign land again this year! I haven't been home for the New Year for twelve years. Imagine how unfortunate this is!

Speaking of which, this is the second time I have celebrated the New Year, because we have already passed a Gregorian New Year. However, the Gregorian New Year is just a matter of government offices hanging up flags, and the common people still celebrate the New Year at the end of the lunar year, no matter how you say that the lunar calendar has long been reduced to a "废历" (waste calendar). The old customs that have been followed for thousands of years cannot be abolished by a piece of paper order. Having said that, schools force classes, and elementary school students don't have time to run out to play, which naturally detracts from the New Year. In addition, the recession in Guangzhou this year makes the New Year less lively than in previous years. However, in the eyes of us "waijiangren" (people from other provinces), the New Year in Guangzhou is still lively, indeed much livelier than our hometown.

The most interesting thing is the flower market. From the 24th or 25th day of the twelfth lunar month, many flower stalls are set up on both sides of the street, selling fresh flowers. In our hometown, every household inserts evergreen cypress for the New Year. Cantonese people like to offer fresh flowers. This shows that the degree of Westernization in Guangzhou is much more advanced than in our small inland cities. Some flower stalls are specially built, with a wooden frame with layers, and many small flower pots are placed on each layer; some do not use flower pots. The people selling flowers insert the broken flower branches into bottles, with all kinds of bottles, from Shaoxing wine jars to glass bottles from pharmacies. This Yonghan North Road, where cars are like flowing water and horses are like dragons, suddenly becomes a beautiful garden, with buds of peony and various roses, foreign chrysanthemums, camellias, kumquats, ink orchids, everything, but red plums, daffodils, and "hanging bell flowers" are the most numerous. Some flower branches stand there taller than people. They are chopped from the trunk of the tree, and many tender buds are hung on them.

The flower market not only sells flowers, but also other small businesses take this opportunity to earn some money for the New Year. There are a few antique stalls, with some old goods piled up in a mess. They are really far inferior to the antiques displayed at the Beijing Changdian Temple Fair. Therefore, wealthy patrons walk past these stalls without even glancing at them. There are also people selling vases, with many vases on the ground, each with an "antique flavor", but the era is probably the 22nd year of the Republic of China. It is said that there is a place near Guangzhou that specializes in making antique bottles. The second is the children selling "lai see envelopes", spending a dime can buy three or four bundles of this mud gold printed small red envelope bag - this is used for the New Year's reward money. There are also many people selling almanacs, which naturally refers to the "廢歷" (waste calendar), because ordinary calendars are the patent of major bookstores, and small businesses have no share.

From the 24th or 25th day of the twelfth lunar month, there are more and more people coming and going on the street. Many of them are here to watch for nothing. "Old Cantonese" always wait until the 30th night to buy flowers, because the flower stalls are rushing to close the market and the prices are cheaper. On the 30th night, as soon as I finished eating, I ran to the street. The streets are full of people, and the sidewalks on both sides are unbearably crowded. There are also many tourists in the center of the street. The cars honk and can't move a step. Cantonese people come to buy flowers at this time. Here, a fashionable girl is holding a pot of daffodils with buds in her hand; there, an old man is holding a branch of cinnabar plum; many people buy "hanging bell flowers", how beautiful the flowers that bloom are! I walked half of Yonghan Road and it took me half an hour, which reminded me of watching the "Flower Festival" in my hometown on March 3rd when I was a child. Chinese people love to watch the excitement everywhere is the same.

On the first day of the first lunar month, I got up early in the morning and ran to the street. It was quiet, and the ground was covered with firecracker paper. Cantonese people originally love to set off firecrackers, and they want to set them off to their heart's content during the New Year. Some of the shops on both sides of the road have their doors closed, and red paper strips with the words "Seven Stars Shining, Magpie Entering the Door" are pasted on the doors; some have their doors half open and half closed, and we can see people playing cards inside. A group of wild children surrounded a stall selling toys. The people selling light air balloons are busy setting up glass bottles, a few drops of sulfuric acid, three or four zinc sheets, and in a while, the rubber bag gradually grows larger, and the people watching next to it feel surprised. "Selling red pigs" is called everywhere on the street, mud piggy banks, this is a lucky item, buying them can make you rich. There are also people selling clams, carrying burdens and selling them from house to house. Cantonese people eat clams during the New Year, just like Italians eat eels during Christmas. Although my hometown is also on the coast, there is no such custom.

As for how Cantonese people spend the New Year at home, if I am still here next year, I will tell you then.

Editorial Office

This publication now intends to solicit local news reports describing customs, habits, landscapes, people, scenic spots, historical sites, anecdotes, interesting facts, etc. from various places at home and abroad. The writing must be clear, fluent, and generous; the length should preferably not be too long. Once adopted, the remuneration will be especially generous. However, manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published or not. Please do not attach postage stamps to the manuscripts.

The Diary of Mary Macklinav by Steppen Leacock Translated by Ye Zi

Beginning! Don't you often look in the mirror?... As for me, I like to stare at my shadow in the mirror for a long time. When my maid Ninizhika or my servant Yakubov passes behind me, they always think I'm crazy. However, I'm not really crazy.

I am seventeen years old.

X X X X X X X X

The next day - while walking, I saw a flower. She was fantasizing on the branch. It was a lilac. I asked her if my heart had never known love. She replied: Yes.

On the way back, I saw a green onion again. Someone crushed his roots. He lay sadly on the road. Ah! How painful he must be!... I hid him in my arms. All night long, he rested by my pillow. I cried.

X X X X X X X X

Another day - my soul felt the hunger of love. Why don't I love someone?

I don't love Alexi, Alexi Soyevich either, although I will marry him within this month.

X X X X X X X X

The day after tomorrow - why do people confine me indoors? I can't stand it anymore! Why do they stop me from committing suicide again? Last night, I did a new experiment again. I put a bottle of sulfuric acid on the table in the bedroom. This morning, the bottle of sulfuric acid was still there. But I didn't die. It's terrible!

X X X X X X X X

The next day - I saw a cabbage on the road. He lay under a plow. He was injured by stones by those naughty children. I wanted to save him... Beside him, there was an egg, also lifeless... I cried.

X X X X X X X X

Economic Supplement

Published every Monday, Issue 61

After the Implementation of Japanese-American Controls

— Bing Yu

The implementation of the Japanese Rice Control Law was outlined in general terms in Issue 47 of this publication. What are its effects? This is a matter of concern to those in our country who are concerned about the food supply. Therefore, this article briefly describes the situation of the Japanese government's handling of rice after November of last year, along with its increases, decreases, and changes, as a reference for us to discuss controlled food.

Since the promulgation of the Japanese Rice Control Law, the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry and the Ministry of Colonial Affairs jointly held a Rice Advisory Committee on December 6 of last year, and also consulted with the Ministry of Finance to proceed with the policy. The grain storage plan was then established, totaling ten million koku of grain in Japan's mainland and colonies. The outline is as follows: (A) Japanese Mainland: (1) The mainland will store six million koku of grain produced this year, but depending on the situation at the time, storage may continue, and new grain produced in the ninth year (of Showa, i.e., 1934) may also be stored. (2) Storage will be subsidized with incentive money. (3) In addition to the incentive money, low-interest financing will be available. (4) The storage period is one year, until the autumn of next year. Disposal will be subject to a permit system. (5) Even after one year, sales will not be allowed if the rice price does not reach a substantial amount. (6) For the purpose of grain storage, 450 state-run warehouses will be built nationwide, with free storage. The storage capacity of the warehouses will be 10 warehouses capable of holding 100,000 koku each, 40 warehouses capable of holding 50,000 koku each, and 1,400 warehouses capable of holding between 1,000 and 5,000 koku each. (7) In addition, small warehouses will be established in units of ten villages or towns, to be built nationwide, funded by landlords, as a reserve for famine relief. (B) Colonies: (1) Korea will store 3 million koku, and Taiwan will store 1 million koku. (2) The government will provide incentive money. (3) Low-interest financing will be available. (4) The storage period will be a relatively long period, and disposal will also be subject to a permit system. (5) Various new warehouses will also be established in Korea and Taiwan. (6) Korea will start from the preparatory period, and Taiwan will implement it from the first harvest of this year.

As for the method of storing six million koku of grain in the Japanese mainland, the result of the national conference of directors of internal affairs of each prefecture was as follows: (A) Implementation Guidelines: (1) Approximately six million koku of grain produced in the mainland in Showa 8 (1933) will be stored autonomously by farmers. (2) The government will adapt to the local conditions to have prefectures, cities, towns, villages, industrial associations, agricultural associations, etc., store the grain. (3) For the storage of grain, a corresponding subsidy will be given in accordance with the rice storage incentive regulations, taking into account interest, storage fees, transportation costs, and other items. (4) The grain shall not be sold unless it rises to 15% above the minimum rice price. (5) If it is deemed necessary to store the grain after April of Showa 9 (next year), storage warehouses will be built in accordance with local conditions, and subsidies may be given to borrowers. (6) Storage of the aforementioned grain will be free of charge, but a portion of the handling fee will be subsidized. (7) The stored grain shall not be sold until the end of the rice year, but subsidies for a fixed amount may be given for disposal of damaged, reduced, deteriorated, or stale grain after storage has begun. (8) A fixed amount of subsidy will be given for the inspection and supervision costs of each prefecture. (9) The proportional amount of grain stored in each prefecture will be allocated from the six million koku. (B) Grain Storage Method: (1) Seeds must be carefully selected to remove any foreign matter. (2) They must be baked and dried to be suitable for long-term storage, but in areas where it is not easy to dry them thoroughly, efforts should be made to dry them as much as possible, and attention should be paid to their condition. (3) Grain that meets the first and second requirements will generally be classified into three grades of standard grain. The classification of standard grain will be determined by each prefecture, and prices will be differentiated according to variety. (4) For storage methods, mixed storage should be used as much as possible, but the degree of dryness of the grain, local customs, and other circumstances should be considered when selecting bag packaging or bulk stacking. When packaging is used, hemp bags or straw bags should be used. (5) Grain should be handled by weight, and the weight should exclude packaging material, and efforts should be made to unify it as much as possible.

According to the survey conducted by the Japanese Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, the number of rice harvests for this year (Showa 8, i.e., 1933) increased by 5,573,332 koku compared to the previous year, and also increased by 5,495,094 koku compared to the previous five years, approximately at 66 million koku.

Showa 3 (1928): 60,303,089

Showa 4 (1929): 59,557,694

Showa 5 (1930): 66,875,535

Showa 6 (1931): 55,215,263

Showa 7 (1932): 60,390,098

Five-year average: 60,468,336

Since the harvest number of rice storage is fixed, this number is used to calculate the supply and demand situation in Showa 9 (next year), and during the lean season, the remaining rice should be more than 16 million koku, so there is a concern that this year's rice is in surplus. On the one hand, there is a desire to purchase to maintain the grain price. Although the official price has been drafted, it is still difficult to be appropriate. The key is still the amount of rice production costs. According to the survey conducted by the Kurashiki City Agricultural Association, the production costs of rice are as follows: (A) Revenue: 3 koku of brown rice is 66 yuan, 1.8 sho of broken rice, 140 kan (approximately 980 catties in our country) of rice straw is 3.36 yuan, 140 catties of rice husk is 0.3 yuan, and secondary income is 4.46 yuan, totaling 70.47 yuan. (B) Expenditure: Direct production cost is 27.35 yuan, including 3 sho of seed cost is 0.39 yuan, fertilizer is 7.16 yuan, labor cost is 15.3 people is 16.8 yuan, various material costs are approximately 1 yuan, livestock cost is 2 yuan, indirect production cost is 37.68 yuan, including agricultural tool cost is 2.3 yuan, building cost is 1.25 yuan, various taxes are 4.66 yuan, and land capital interest is 29.46 yuan, totaling 65.03 yuan. The income and expenditure offset each other, with a surplus of 5.4 yuan, that is, the actual production cost of 1 koku is 21.68 yuan, and the selling price of 1 koku is 25.49 yuan, but according to the provisional minimum price of 22.7 yuan, there is only a profit of 1.2 yuan. Also, according to the calculation of the Agricultural Association, among 860 farm households, the production cost per koku, excluding 82 households with less than 18 yuan and more than 33 yuan, the production cost of the other 778 households is 4.48 yuan for direct production cost and 3.32 yuan for indirect production cost, totaling 7.8 yuan, which is 25.21 yuan per koku. Therefore, the Rice Control Committee decided on the official price as follows: (1) The standard maximum price is 30.5 yuan. (2) The standard minimum price is 23.3 yuan. However, the Imperial Agricultural Association and the political parties were quite dissatisfied. The Seiyukai's intention was to advocate that the minimum price should be raised to 25 yuan. The Agricultural Association believed that the minimum rice price, the production cost per koku for self-cultivating farmers was 23.73 yuan, plus transportation and miscellaneous expenses of 1.48 yuan, should be above 25.21 yuan, so it must be raised to this number or above. Afterwards, it was finally passed according to the original plan. In the beginning of the implementation of the control, farmers were all watching and waiting, and almost no one dared to sell. When the second harvest volume was announced, it was 270,000 koku more than the first time (65,963,000 koku), the price index gradually declined again, and the government's seasonal purchases were delayed, coupled with the pressure of new rice, the rice price gradually showed a downward trend. This is because the harvest in the Japanese mainland has been 65,963,000 koku, the import of rice from Taiwan and Korea is 13 million koku, plus the current inventory of 9.07 million koku, totaling 87,970,000 koku. By the time of the lean season next year, after deducting the consumption of 71,540,000 koku (calculated based on a population of 66,860,000 and a per capita annual consumption of 1.06 koku per day), the surplus is more than 10 million koku. Therefore, since the Rice Control Committee resolved to increase the provisional price by 0.6 yuan, requests for the sale of rice to the government have suddenly increased everywhere. It is heard that from December 20 to 21, it reached 826,615 bags, that is, 330,000 koku, and farmers were deeply afraid that they would not be able to maintain the price of 23 yuan, and those who sold rushed to it. It is estimated that since the implementation of the control, the total number of applications has reached 1.33 million koku, resulting in the government's inability to cope. In addition, at the end of last year, farmers were eager to obtain money, and the amount of sales increased even more. According to past practice, the average monthly sales at the end of each year are around 100,000 koku. Since the promulgation of the statistics law, the rice price has been weakening day by day, and farmers are generally pessimistic, so the request to sell is even more difficult to prevent. Other things, such as the import of Korean rice into Japan, are also more than in previous years. In Showa 7 (1932), the import of Korean rice was 7,503,000 koku, and this year it increased by approximately 300,000 koku, and the Tokyo market has already fallen from 24 yuan to 23.75 yuan. Last November, the highest price was 24.97 yuan, and in less than a month, it suddenly plummeted by 1.23 yuan. It is estimated that the request to sell rice at the end of March will be less than 2 million koku. However, the Japanese government has neither unlimited funds nor warehouse facilities. Therefore, in order to maintain the control law and relieve rural areas, the government had to reluctantly cope. This is still in regard to the situation at the end of last year.

Japan strictly implements rice control, which has been discussed by the Rice Committee members and approved by the Advisory Conference. It stipulates that the Japanese mainland store 6 million koku, Korea store 3 million koku, and Taiwan store 1 million koku, and there are funds to provide financing. Interest during the storage period and transportation costs of storage warehouses are given incentive money, and free storage is also available. 1,450 storage warehouses are built throughout the country. The construction of storage warehouses initially adopted urban concentration, with 60 large warehouses with a storage capacity of 100,000 koku being built in each prefecture throughout the country. Later, after referring to opinions from various aspects, the storage incentive plan was submitted to the Advisory Conference, and a combination of centralized and decentralized approaches was used. Ten warehouses with a storage capacity of 100,000 koku were built in central metropolitan areas, 40 warehouses with a storage capacity of 50,000 koku were built in small and medium-sized cities, and 1,400 small warehouses with a storage capacity of between 1,000 and 5,000 koku were built in villages and towns throughout the country. These warehouses are all built by the government. Farmers' grain should all be entrusted to government storage warehouses for safekeeping. The government believes that if farmers themselves use industrial associations or grain storage associations to build small-scale warehouses in rural villages and manage them autonomously, it will not be completely appropriate. It is better to have the government operate them, which can be more unified. However, its biggest drawback is that the grain cannot be sold unless it rises to 15% above the standard minimum price. If there is no opportunity to sell it by the end of the rice year, the government has no choice but to compensate the storers for the cost of damage and deterioration, thus increasing the burden on the national treasury. Moreover, all the stored grain is managed by the government, not by the farmers themselves, which hinders the spirit of rural autonomy. Therefore, the Japanese Seiyukai advocates that the grain storage system should refer to the old rural storage system (charitable granaries), and organize grain storage associations in villages and tribes in the spirit of mutual assistance between neighbors, so as to have the functions of famine relief and supply regulation; at the same time, it can be divided into mandatory storage and voluntary storage, and the development of a farmer-autonomous storage system can also be expected. This was ultimately opposed by the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, and the original plan was still implemented. Unexpectedly, the Japanese Ministry of Finance halved the budget of the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, and on the other hand, there were different treatments in terms of the interests of landlords, self-cultivating farmers, and tenants from the standpoint of grain storage. As a result, accusations arose. According to the Tokyo Jiji Shinpo on January 13, the amount of rice sold by farm households throughout the country has reached 3.8 million koku. If it reaches the end of the old lunar year, there will be 200,000 to 300,000 koku of sales every day. The Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry expects that it will have to increase to 8 million koku within this year's rice year. However, the remaining funds of the special account for rice supply and demand regulation are 420 million yuan, and the maximum amount of purchases per year is only 6 million koku. Therefore, in light of the current situation, it has reached the amount for two years. The effectiveness of the control law is almost in a state of danger. Moreover, the minimum price of rice still cannot be maintained in principle, and the government's financial damage is becoming more and more exhausted. When the Japanese parliament convened this year, the members immediately questioned whether there were any countermeasures to improve the situation. And the rice harvest in Japan again exceeded expectations, reaching a huge amount of 70 million koku, and the rice price was in a situation where it could not be maintained, and the government also felt that the rice finances could not cope with this situation. Since the parliament has questioned it, if no other compensation is planned, the political parties will inevitably propose rural rice countermeasures separately, forcing the government to implement them. Therefore, Agriculture Minister Goto and Prime Minister Saito discussed the results and decided to propose new countermeasures: (1) increase the operating funds of the rice department to cope with farmers' sales; (2) effectively manage rice in the two colonies of Korea and Taiwan; (3) amend the current rice control law; (4) decide to take an overseas dumping policy, and first transport more than 10 million koku of the remaining rice of more than 10 million koku to the Yangtze River area and various commercial ports in North China to sell at reduced prices, and the losses will be compensated by the government. In addition, the Taiwan government will transport 500,000 koku of its Penglai rice to various important commercial ports in Guangdong and Fujian provinces for dumping, and the losses will be shared by Taiwanese farmers and the Taiwan government. As for the implementation methods of the aforementioned items (2) and (3), it seems to have been confirmed by the Tokyo telecommunications of the China United News Agency on February 4. Farmers in Taiwan and Korea, as people of a subjugated country, are bound to be sacrificed everywhere. In the end, they are the meat on the chopping board of the Japanese people, and our Chinese farmers, because the country is weak and has no resistance, also suffer the misfortune of the pond fish and suffer the harm of Japanese rice dumping. Isn't it very sad! The China United News Agency telecommunications are attached below.

The Japanese government has decided to sacrifice the people of the two colonies of Taiwan and Korea for the benefit of the landlords and tenants of Japan because rice harvests have made life extremely difficult for landlords and tenants. It is very determined to change its rice policy, then listen to the demands of the Minseito and Seiyukai parties to amend the Rice Control Law. Its purpose is to prevent the transportation of rice from the two colonies of Taiwan and Korea to Japan, and compete with Japanese rice, causing the market price of Japanese rice to fall, in order to maintain the market price of Japanese rice, that is, to maintain the official price and avoid farmers from shaking. The colonial rice management issue is being discussed by the Ministries of Agriculture and Colonial Affairs and the governments of the two colonies. However, the two governments still disagree with the demands of the home country because they fear increasing the resistance of the ruled people, and strive for management methods to reduce the degree of sacrifice. However, Agriculture Minister Goto firmly represents the interests of the ruling nation, and decided to submit the colonial rice management plan and the rice amendment plan to the cabinet meeting on the 6th, to have the cabinet meeting pass them, and then force the governments of the two colonies to recognize them. It is heard that the Agriculture Minister's countermeasures are: (1) colonial rice will be managed by the government, (2) colonial areas will reduce rice production and promote the conversion to miscellaneous grains, (3) colonial rice export permit system, (4) colonial areas will implement special rice, etc. It is said that one of the four plans will be implemented.

Although the above-mentioned countermeasures have not yet been submitted to the parliament due to Agriculture Minister Goto's illness, they will not be implemented immediately. However, the Japanese government has always had a strategy of avoiding names and seeking substance, or even implementing the results of the cabinet meeting first to avoid people's ears and eyes. The Japanese rice harvest has become a fact (including Taiwan and Korea), and the disaster of a bumper harvest is also a unanimous view of the Japanese government and the public. If the Japanese government wants to protect the livelihood of Japanese farmers, it has no choice but to accept the remaining rice, or the rice that is temporarily trapped by financial resources and cannot be stored, according to the aforementioned method. After acceptance: if those who come are not refused, the financial resources will inevitably be exhausted at times, and if they are refused, the farmers' riot will arise, and the government is in danger of collapse, so the only way is to dump overseas in order to vent. Looking around the world, the most convenient country for dumping is China. Although China is said to have cheap rice, is its cause a bumper harvest! Is it due to uneven regulation! Is it due to the poverty of the people! This is quite complicated, and I am afraid it is not as simple as the cause of cheap Japanese rice. Moreover, Japan has concessions in China to hide it, and the navy to cover it. If dumping merchants have losses, the government has resolved to compensate them, so dumping in China is only a matter of time.

According to the current rice price, if it is impossible for Japanese rice to be sold in China, it is because the losses are too great, but what about the price of Taiwanese rice? As for the saying that Japanese rice dumping is Japanese counter-propaganda, using "exit" as "entry," it is no different from a fool talking in his sleep, wanting to cover it up. Unless Japanese rice cancels its dumping method, it will ultimately target China. It will inevitably pay attention to South China first, and Fujian in South China is more convenient than Guangdong. Fujian is adjacent to Taiwan, and Taiwanese rice has always been used by the people of Fujian Province to make up for it. The second is Guangdong. In the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930), Japanese rice came to Shanghai for dumping, but was blocked by the people of Shanghai, and turned to Hong Kong to enter Guangdong. The next best choice is Tianjin, but Tianjin has tariffs, and competition is more difficult. The Yangtze River area is a rice-producing area, and there is originally no need for sales, but if the rice price rises to more than ten yuan, Taiwanese rice may already be among the local rice. At present, the only helpless countermeasure is to urge the two provinces of Fujian and Guangdong to levy tariffs on imported foreign rice in accordance with the customs tariff regulations, which may slightly reduce its momentum, but I am still afraid that it will not be fully effective.

Comparison of the Advantages and Disadvantages of Ordinary Checks and Limited-Amount Checks

— Pan Hengqin

Regarding the matter of limited-amount checks, I have repeatedly written articles for publication in newspapers, forgetting my own shallowness. This type of check can directly avoid the evils of bounced checks and altered checks, and indirectly has the possibility of promoting the circulation of negotiable instruments. Although it cannot be said to be a perfect solution, it is still worth studying and promoting at a time when the circulation of negotiable instruments is not widespread and social fraud abounds. Some contemporary scholars believe that limited-amount checks, if the limited amount is too high, it is still difficult to avoid alteration; and it is believed that it is only suitable for small-amount depositors. In my opinion, although it is still difficult to avoid the evils of alteration if the limited amount is too high, it is still slightly better than those without a limited amount. It seems that we should not give up eating for fear of choking. As for the promotion of limited-amount checks, although it was initiated for depositors with weak credit, the actual application does not necessarily have to be limited to depositors with weak credit. Even commercial transactions are not necessarily unsuitable. However, the principle can be that depositors voluntarily use them. However, the mentality of depositors when issuing checks is that they all hope that their checks will be trusted by others and easy to circulate; as for the mentality of the payee, they all hope that the checks they receive are indeed reliable. Those who can have this effect, except for those who deal with large banks, limited-amount checks are almost equipped with it. Limited-amount checks are issued to depositors by the bank according to the deposit amount, which actually contains a guarantee nature. The wider the circulation, the more convenient the transaction. In other words, the number of returned checks is less between the issuer and recipient of limited-amount checks, while the number of returned checks is more between the issuer and recipient of ordinary checks. Even if the procedure for issuing limited-amount checks may be slightly more cumbersome than issuing ordinary checks, merchants value credit most, and procedures are secondary. If issuing a check can enhance the credit of the negotiable instrument, even if it requires slightly more procedures, it should not be declined. The fact that ordinary checks have a stamp with the words "Please exchange for a promissory note" is one example. Moreover, whether the procedure is convenient or not is a relative rather than an absolute matter, and it is completely a matter of habit. After it has been implemented for a long time, it will no longer be a problem. The key is for the bank to be good at adapting to the circumstances. Now, I will list and analyze the comparison of the advantages and disadvantages of ordinary checks and limited-amount checks below for research.

Ordinary Check　　　　　　　　Limited-Amount Check

Issuer Advantage Freedom to fill in the amount　　 (1) The payee is more at ease and welcomes the receipt because this type of check has a guarantee nature. (2) Not easy to be altered.

Disadvantage (1) The payee is afraid of bounced checks and may not welcome it. (2) Easy to be altered. Limited amount can be filled in.

Person

Bank Advantage Simple procedure for issuing checks to depositors. No mistaken payment of bounced or altered checks.

Disadvantage Prevent mistaken payment of bounced or altered checks. The procedure for issuing checks to depositors is more cumbersome.

Recipient Advantage In addition to the issuer's seal being inconsistent or lost, there is no risk of bounced or altered checks.

Disadvantage In addition to the issuer's seal being inconsistent or lost, there is also a risk of bounced or altered checks.

Person

The above-mentioned advantages and disadvantages are clear. Furthermore, ordinary checks can be reported as lost if they are lost due to fire, theft, or loss, but limited-amount checks, because they circulate for a longer period of time, are more beneficial to the issuer in terms of interest than ordinary checks before they are exchanged at the bank.

Hubei Donation and Tax Records (Continued, Part 2) Xue Wuying

Six: Luotian

The estimated number of donations and taxes in Luotian County is about thirty-six types:

(1) Land Tax: For every ten shi of land, a land tax of 1 mace, 1 fen, and 3 li of silver is levied, equivalent to $0.158 in silver dollars, with an annual revenue of $17,385. (2) Grain Tribute: For every ten shi of land, a grain tribute of 5 sheng, 6 he, and 6 shao is levied, equivalent to $0.158 in silver dollars, with an annual revenue of $17,266. (3) Purchase Contract Tax: 9% per dollar, with an annual revenue of $9,000. (4) Mortgage Contract Tax: 6% per dollar, with an annual revenue of $6,000. (5) Contract Paper Fee: $0.50 per sheet, with an annual revenue of $500. (6) Long-term Brokerage License Fee: $10 per license, with an annual revenue of $260. (7) Short-term Brokerage License Fee: $20 per license per year, with an annual revenue of $120. (8) Slaughter Tax: $0.40 per head, with an annual revenue of $6,400. (9) Stamp Tax: Approximately $600 annually. (10) Business Tax: Approximately $2,400 annually. (11) Tobacco and Alcohol Tax: $3.60 per shi for miscellaneous wine, $0.60 per shi for rice wine, with an annual revenue of $900. (12) Land Tax Surtax: A surtax of 2 jiao, 9 fen, and 9 li is levied per tael, with an annual revenue of $3,713. (13) Rural Pacification Donation: An additional 20% is levied based on the land tax and grain tribute, with an annual revenue of $6,930. (14) Educational Donation Surtax on Land Tax: $0.262 is levied per tael of silver, and $0.262 per shi of rice, totaling $3,900 annually. (15) Agency Fee Surtax on Land Tax: Collected as educational expenses, $0.042 is levied per large assessment, totaling $1,200 annually. (16) Tare Weight Fee Surtax on Land Tax: $0.056 is levied per large assessment, totaling $1,500 annually. (17) Self-Government Donation Surtax on Land Tax: $0.35 is levied per tael of silver, and $0.70 per shi of rice, totaling $6,700 annually. (18) Party Affairs Donation Surtax on Land Tax: $0.598 is levied per shi of rice, with an annual revenue of $2,900. Although this item is named the Party Affairs Donation, it is used for the expenses of the Military Transportation Agency and the Farmers' Training Institute of the Third District. (19) Voucher Donation: $0.033 per voucher, with an annual revenue of $1,848. (20) Land Tax Fine: One-tenth to one-twentieth, with an annual revenue of $1,000. (21) Educational Donation Surtax on Contract Tax: $0.02 is levied per dollar, with an annual revenue of $1,600. (22) Party Affairs Donation Surtax on Tax: The purpose is the same as the Party Affairs Donation Surtax on Land Tax, $0.02 is levied per dollar, approximately $1,600 annually. (23) Public Security Donation Surtax on Contract Tax: $0.02 is levied per dollar, totaling $1,600 annually. (24) Self-Government Donation Surtax on Contract Tax: $0.011 is levied per dollar, for the expenses of the District Office, totaling $880 annually. (25) Guard Donation Surtax on Contract Tax: $0.007 is levied per dollar, for the expenses of the Rural Pacification Committee, with an annual revenue of $560. (26) Charity Donation Surtax on Contract Tax: $0.004 is levied per dollar, for the expenses of the Orphanage and Smallpox Bureau, totaling $320 annually. (27) Industry Donation Surtax on Contract Tax: $0.007 is levied per dollar, for the expenses of the Nursery, totaling $560 annually. (28) Contract Tax Fine: A fine of one to three times the contract price is imposed, approximately $25 annually. (29) Brokerage Tax Educational Donation Surtax: $10 per license, with an annual revenue of $300. (30) Slaughter Surtax for Educational Donation: $0.10 per head, with an annual revenue of $1,000. (31) Official Intermediary Donation: $3 per year for each person in each small district to obtain a license, totaling $180 annually, used for financial expenses. (32) Cattle Broker Donation: $50 per year in multiple villages, $40 in average villages, and $30 in abundant villages to obtain a license, totaling $120 annually, used for financial expenses. (33) Gentry and Wealthy Donation: Apportioned to each district for team rations, totaling $30,000 annually. (34) Gentry and Wealthy Loan: Apportioned to each district for team rations, totaling $40,000 annually. (35) Aircraft Donation: $1,200 apportioned to each district. (36) Special Loan: Used for team maintenance fees, district office maintenance fees, and rural pacification maintenance fees, totaling $3,400 annually.

In addition, there are many temporary apportionments in each village, such as the cook donation, courier post fee, Baojia donation, etc., with numerous items, amounting to nearly three dollars or more per household per month.

X X X

Overall, from the above counties, we can see the heavy burden of donations and taxes in rural areas. Analyzing it, we can obtain the following phenomena:

(1) Numerous items: As listed, each county can have more than forty types.

(2) Many surtaxes: Almost every tax has a surtax, and the types of surtaxes are extremely complex.

(3) Many miscellaneous taxes: The so-called gentry and wealthy donations, Baojia donations, etc., have particularly increased in recent years.

(4) Many collecting agencies: For example, in Luotian, there are always four or five or more collecting agencies.

(5) Much embezzlement: Many taxes, many collecting agencies, then there must be much embezzlement, especially miscellaneous taxes and temporary apportionments, which are indeed opportunities for local bullies to make money.

(6) Much consumption: And very little is used for production, even charity and public welfare expenses are rare, mostly for government and security expenses.

Since donations and taxes in rural areas are so heavy, the high-sounding talk of rural recovery is really too far off. It is hoped that the authorities will pay attention to the lack.

Securities: The First Week After the Holiday Saw Many New Highs in the Bond Market

Market prices were at their peak, and a reaction gradually emerged at the weekend.

In the week of February 19th to 24th, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange experienced the first week of trading in the national bond market after the Lunar New Year holiday. Following a long nine-day break, the situation stabilized and sentiment was firm. The market opened on a bullish note on the 19th. Due to the New Year, only half-day trading sessions were held each morning, with two transactions. The atmosphere was generally cheerful, with more buying than selling. With only four days left in the February futures, the short sellers were somewhat panicked. The market price rose sharply, and the bullish opening became a natural trend. Most bond prices reached new highs. The best-performing bond was the Disbandment Bond, which surged by more than one dollar, reaching a high of $69.85, breaking the previous high of $69.20 on July 19, 1933. On Tuesday, both long and short positions wrestled with each other, and the market price stabilized, with highs and lows alternating. On Wednesday, the short squeeze continued, with the long positions holding firm and the market price rising by another two or three jiao. Thursday was the last day of February, and except for the Disbandment Bond, which eased by about three jiao due to the long positions rolling over, the remaining bonds continued to rise by three to seven jiao. On Friday, only the March contract was traded, and the initial rally remained strong. Most bonds, up to the Salt Tax Bond, reached new highs, marking one of the highest market levels of the year. Most had already surpassed the highest records of the previous year. However, due to the frantic selling of the Short-Term Gold Bond on the 4th and 20th, it alone turned downward. With sentiment slightly weakened, it immediately showed signs of weakness. On Saturday, rumors spread, and many long positions were liquidated. The Disbandment Bond 19 was sold off significantly, falling by more than one dollar, while other bonds also fell by a small amount. As a result of the week's market performance, the February contracts rose by several jiao to $1.78, while the March contracts rose by only one or two jiao to half a dollar. Due to the high market levels, a reversal was likely. Rumors were insignificant, and the future was not expected to see major changes. The total trading volume for the week was $73,182,000, including $22,000 in spot trading and $73,160,000 in futures trading. The highs, lows, rises, and falls are compared below. (Unit: Dollar, Trading Unit: Hundred Dollars). Starting tomorrow, full-day trading with four sessions will resume, and the April futures will also be added.

Yarn and Cotton: American Cotton Seems to Have a Rebound Tendency

Yesterday's American cotton market was mixed, with concerns of a rebound. It initially strengthened due to buying by traders, but later weakened due to the weakness of Wall Street. As a result, the spot price remained unchanged, while the futures price fell by one to seven points per pound. Liverpool cotton spot prices fell by four points, and futures prices fell by three to four points. The Bombay cotton market initially strengthened due to short covering, but later changed due to profit-taking, resulting in a weakening. As a result, the Pingar remained unchanged, the Omra fell by 1 rupee and 7.5 annas, and the White Karachi fell by 1.5 rupees. The original telegram is on the left (telegram of the 24th):
