Shanghai Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

New Books Sold by the Pound

— Wen Li

A certain bookstore in Shanghai is selling at a great discount, new books are sold at one dollar for three and a half pounds, regardless of the content value of the new books, good or bad, works by famous writers or unknown writers, they are bundled together and priced according to the weight of the paper, just like selling fish and vegetables in the small vegetable market, priced by the pound. This news is already thought-provoking enough. A certain bookstore gave the newly published literary books to its peers for five yuan per dan before the New Year, and the peers bought them and said it was because of the face of their boss. The downturn in the new book industry, along with the value of culture and academics, has plummeted! Alas!

The publication of a new book first goes through the writer's exhaustive efforts, thinking and planning, and then writing it out. Secondly, the typesetting and printing workers have to print it out several times with trouble. The human effort alone is considerable, even if the new book has no value, it should not be sold by the pound according to the weight of the paper. Moreover, some paper prices are more than three and a half pounds worth one dollar, or one dan worth five dollars, this new book market price really gives the writers a feeling of swallowing cold air.

Literary people, except for those who help the rulers, those who make a living by selling articles are regarded by the society as literary beggars. Although they think they are noble, their social status is inferior and inferior. Now, the new books of literary people are sold by the pound, losing both fame and profit. Alas, the end of literary people has arrived!

Articles have never been valuable since ancient times. Poetry is called "carving insects and small skills", and novels are referred to as "street talk and alley discussions". Therefore, ancient people used aliases and pen names when writing books. Now, writers are raising their voices, but in this highly commodified modern society, the impact of the market downturn means that writers' works will inevitably encounter the fate of being worthless. It is no wonder that the poet Zhu Xiang committed suicide by drowning.

New books are sold by the pound, and I dare to predict that from now on there will be many writers who follow in Zhu Xiang's footsteps. Economic pressure is already enough to take people's lives, not to mention that the real social environment gives people unlimited depression and pain in spirit?

I Think of Him

— Boer

I remember that before I met him, I unintentionally offended him. A friend, T, invited me to Xinguang [Theater], and since T was also his friend, we unexpectedly ended up watching a movie together in the same theater. The movie that day was a martial arts film, without much meaning, but there was a very fierce lion, or perhaps a leopard, in it. When we came out of the theater, T confidently asked me to guess, saying:

"Do you know if it's a lion or a leopard?" I replied that it was a leopard. He said I was completely wrong, that it was just a lioness whose appearance was similar to a leopard. I insisted, "Fool! Isn't it obviously a leopard?" T was even more unconvinced and had to find a third party to prove it. The third party was that Mr. Meng, who, like T, said it was a lion. This really infuriated me, and I quickly interjected, "He's a fool too!" Because he didn't know me, he didn't say anything even though I had called him a fool for no reason. I didn't think that such an ordinary sentence would offend him. In fact, when I call people fools, it's not out of malice or contempt. Sometimes, I even like to call someone I adore a fool. After Mr. Meng and I became acquainted, I didn't think of him as a fool, and in fact, he wasn't. But I called him a fool several times. Once, he was very unhappy and about to get angry because I called him that. I said to him, "You're not a fool to begin with, but now you really are. Just because I call you that, does it mean you'll really become a fool? Really a fool!"

Mr. Meng originally didn't want to get to know me. One day, he heard people say that where I lived was not good, and the landlord was a bad person, causing me a lot of inconvenience. He wanted to persuade me to move. Because of this, he had to come to my place to meet me. That's how he and I became acquainted and started talking. Judging from this, his motivation for getting to know me can be said to be very simple.

After that, it was not surprising that we would meet, but a certain barrier between men and women was unavoidable. This wasn't due to feudal thinking; I myself found it strange. I interacted with quite a few men, and he had countless girlfriends. I usually didn't feel awkward with friends. I could say whatever I wanted, even my own difficult situations. I wasn't afraid of others knowing. Sometimes, I only had one copper coin left in my pocket, but if I needed to see a friend, I would casually borrow ten cents from them. I didn't like to hide things, be hypocritical, or pretend to be rich. But with Mr. Meng, I couldn't say anything.

As time went on, our feelings for each other were quite good. I didn't need to hide anything from him, but I saw him as a rich man and didn't want to receive his help, so I didn't want him to know that I was down on my luck. But one time, he asked to eat at my house. He wanted to see if the dishes I cooked myself were delicious. Logically, this was a very ordinary thing, but because I didn't have chairs or a table at home, it would be inconvenient to entertain guests, so I couldn't agree to him. But this small request, due to my insistence on refusing, aroused his curiosity. He impolitely waited in my room. As a result, lunch was not ready until 2 p.m. With no other choice, I would rather treat him to a meal outside. This was how we solved a lunch problem, and at the same time, he observed many things about my life that he had never known before. Later, he hoped to understand me more and came up with a plan: he asked to eat at my house every day. He said he had been very poor recently and didn't have money to eat at restaurants. This unbelievable statement really troubled me. The problem wasn't about chairs and tables, but about not having money to buy groceries and rice. This time, I couldn't hide it anymore, and I couldn't find any more money to treat him to meals. Forget it! I could be open about everything. At that time, he took out the only bill in his pocket and asked the landlord's servant to exchange it for small change. Unfortunately, she came back and said, "Sir, the bill can't be used!" How sad we were when we received the bill!

In our friendship, it couldn't help but naturally become closer day by day. He understood me, sympathized with me, and my difficulties swirled in his mind. He sincerely thought of several ways to arrange my life. At the same time, he told me he was leaving Shanghai, and the time was very hurried. After this news reached my ears, although the material needs could be temporarily solved, I suffered a great spiritual trauma. My heart suddenly became cold, and my eyes seemed numb.

Time passed quickly, and he decided on the date of his departure. He told me he would take a car to my place and then go to the ship together. But that day, I waited until 1:45 p.m. and still didn't see him. The ship was scheduled to depart at 3 p.m. I assumed he was too sad and deliberately didn't come to say goodbye. If I had waited patiently, I thought I would never see him again. So, I hurriedly called a rickshaw and drove straight to the dock. Coincidentally, he had just arrived, but it was already late. After his luggage was placed in the cabin, he held my hand and sent me back to the dock. In half a minute, we had to let go of each other's hands. His heart was probably very anxious, and he quickly gave me a farewell kiss on the lips, then flew onto the ship. We parted so hurriedly. I stood at the dock, waiting for his ship to disappear from my sight. I returned home with heavy, monotonous steps. I still remembered him in my heart. Silence! I was very afraid! …

Kindness and Insidiousness

— Where to Go

Someone once said that the kindest animals are the most terrible.

For example, cats. When it's curled up at your feet, its green, glowing pupils narrowed to a slit, and you run your hand over its soft, "Persian rug"-like fur, you'll definitely feel that this animal is truly very gentle, and you can definitely get a most intimate feeling of tenderness from your fingertips. However, you never consider that this small thing has a very poisonous beastly heart and the sharpest claws. And these claws will suddenly extend when you're gently caressing it with goodwill, grabbing your hand and sinking deep into the flesh, causing you to bleed immediately.

Likewise, generally speaking, the treacherous politicians or imperialists in history, none of them lacks this gentle appearance. Originally, a gentle appearance is most suitable for concealing a treacherous intention. Because man-eating tigers and wolves can sometimes be as kind as a "grandmother," and the most poisonous flowers are exceptionally beautiful. However, this kindness is a means of eating people, and the beauty of the flower is a way to entice people to approach it.

As we straightforward people see it, man-eating tigers and wolves should openly show that they are man-eating tigers and wolves, and treacherous politicians should show that they are treacherous. This is greater than those people whose outward appearance is merciful but whose hearts are insidious. For example, Zhang Zuolin was said to be a bandit and frankly admitted that he was a bandit. From a historical perspective, this is greater and more likable than hypocritical and insidious people like Wang Mang. Because this is a display of the most candid human nature, and the thoroughness of this display is worthy of admiration.

Sometimes, when we are with a murderer and a silent monk, listening to the murderer's eloquent speech, hearing him tell all about his motive for killing and everything he felt in his heart, we feel that such a person is not only not scary, but rather very likable. On the contrary, the silent monk, who only faces you with his serene demeanor, occasionally showing a smile that is definitely not genuine, we easily feel that these people are mysterious, and it is easiest to breed suspicion. Therefore, inevitably, we become wary of such people.

And this is a kind of human candor and a kind of human insidiousness.

People who don't hide their state of mind at all are easier to deal with than those who are silent and hide things deeply. The latter is exactly the opposite. Perhaps it's precisely because they are difficult to be dealt with and difficult to be understood that those insidious and treacherous people make their outward appearance exceptionally kind, but their bellies are full of ghosts.

Bad Luck

— Cun

People in the Jiangzhe area have a common saying, "Touching bad luck." When people encounter bad luck, it's never a good thing. I've had so many unlucky things happen to me this year that I can't even remember them all. Today, I encountered it again, and the more I think about it, the more depressed I feel.

Jingwen had asked me to contact a certain editor about something several times, but I always forgot. Today, when I went to Jingwen's place, he brought it up again and said, "Why haven't you contacted him yet?" I was in a good mood, so I called him. That Mr. [Editor], though we weren't exactly close acquaintances, but we had met a few times and even hung out together at the dance hall. Therefore, when I called him, I thought that if I just said what I wanted to say, I could succeed. Unexpectedly, I spoke to him on the phone very happily and politely, but he said in an arrogant tone, "Wait until I connect with Jingwen!" This sentence was already disrespectful, but unexpectedly, he hung up the phone immediately after saying that, without even waiting for me to say another word, or even saying goodbye. This snub really shocked me, I had never encountered such a snub before. When I mentioned it to Jingwen, he pondered for a moment and said, "I forgot to tell you, a few days ago, Lu Shan called and said that some tabloid fabricated rumors saying that she and he were getting married. She said I wrote it. I said I never read tabloids and didn't have that kind of free time. She said if it wasn't me, then it was old Cun who wrote it. I said old Cun doesn't do this kind of thing, I don't have that kind of friend. Today, he probably gave you a snub because of this!" I really touched bad luck, people are blaming me for other people's business. I was incredibly angry at the time, and I immediately wanted to reason with them, but Jingwen stopped me and said, "Wait for me to call Lu Shan, why are you in such a hurry? You fool!" I left Jingwen's place and went home, and the more I thought about it, the angrier I got. I was so polite to them, but I was repaid with ingratitude, and now they're even accusing me of publishing their news in some tabloid. It's not easy to make friends these days, and I'm running into bad luck everywhere.

Smooth Sailing

— Liyue

At the end of the lunar year, I went to a friend's house for a New Year's Eve dinner. In his living room, besides the usual large red-gold character candles and nandina and wintersweet flowers on the altar, there were also two large lotus roots, each more than two feet long, lying on both sides of the altar table. One of the guests pointed to the lotus roots on the table and asked the host what their purpose was. The friend explained: "This is called 'smooth sailing,' and it means hoping that everything will be smooth and accessible everywhere next year, and that you can make money everywhere."

Smooth sailing. If you use the Shanghai dialect, that's "be able to turn around".

Someone said: "In Shanghai, not having money doesn't matter. As long as you can turn around, you can start a business and build a market."

Those who owe hundreds or thousands of dollars are often beaten until their heads are broken and bleeding. Suppose you owe hundreds of thousands or millions of dollars, you are instead carefree, sitting in a car, living in a Western-style house, and the food goes without saying, what is it if not delicacies from land and sea? Let me ask you, where do they get so much money? Of course, they have their own magical powers. If you ask again what this skill is? Let me tell you, this is called being able to turn around, which is smooth sailing.

There are also merchants who traffic in contraband and evade national taxes. No matter how strict the national laws are or how heavy the penalties are, they have clever ways to escape the law. In other respects, boycotting enemy goods, no matter how tight social opinion is, judging from customs import statistics, enemy goods have greatly increased. It can be seen that there are still people doing it on a large scale. And still making a fortune. Of course, their various methods and secrets cannot be done without being able to turn around.

In short. If you can turn around smoothly, no matter what aspect, you can get a lot of face and take a lot of advantage.

Smooth sailing, smooth sailing, Chinese society is circling in smooth sailing.

Amateur Mailbox

Answers to Several Legal Questions (2)

Editor:

I am a young man who graduated from junior high school and has also studied commerce for several years. Now I want to support myself and plan to open a small department store. The store's staff is also being recruited in the newspaper. But I don't know if I need to register if I open this kind of store in the concession, and which agency I should register with? What about in Zhabei? Are there any books I can refer to? I heard from a friend that when opening a store, there are often gangsters who unreasonably demand drinking money, etc. I think you are our guiding teacher, so you won't leave this unanswered, right?

Respectfully wish you, Mr.

Good health!

Sincerely, Lu Lun

Editor's note: When opening a store, whether in the concession or in the Chinese area, you can apply for registration with the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau. Regarding registration procedures, you can purchase and read the book "General Rules for Merchants" from the bookstore for reference. If there are gangsters who take the opportunity to demand from newly opened stores, you can immediately call the police and have them dealt with.

Editor:

My friend met a girlfriend. After repeated visits, the two gradually fell in love. It is said that during their passionate period of love, in addition to sweet kisses, they also engaged in physical intimacy such as semi-naked embraces (of course, he took the initiative). But afterwards, he was blamed by her, saying that he had insulted her and wanted him to find a way to make amends. If they went a step further and got married from then on, it would have been a very beautiful thing, but my friend has been married since he was a child. Although the relationship is not good, he already has children, and he cannot abandon them in principle. Therefore, the two of them have been discussing this without a good solution. Now I want to ask you for him!

(1) If she and his she and both families can agree to marry her as a second wife according to local custom (this custom is said to be common in Guangdong, and it seems to exist in other places as well, that is, one man marries two women, both of whom are called wives, without distinguishing between the principal and secondary wife), can this be permitted by law?

(2) In law and morality, is the crime of destroying virginity only established when sexual intercourse has been completed?

(3) If the above question is true, then how is the completion and non-completion of sexual intercourse distinguished? Please answer the above three questions publicly in the amateur mailbox!

(2) (3) Not necessarily

Brother Mao and Sister Bao Travel the World

— Meng

Novel

Husband and Wife (8)

— Yu Mei

She listened to the sound of footsteps walking out, and listened to the sound of the big door closing tightly. She returned to silence, only hearing a little human voice in the distance. She put a piece of opium on the pipe and squatted on the fire bucket. She bowed her head into a semi-sleeping daze, not knowing how much time had passed.

Suddenly, the big door rang again. She woke up with a start, her heart jumping a little. She asked,

"Who's coming in?" She faced the outside of the room.

"It's me." The answer contained an element of laughter and emotion.

"Slowly, I'll light your way." She nimbly stepped out of the fire bucket and took the lamp out of the room. The man was already outside the door. She smiled at the man who came and asked, "What time is it?"

"It's almost midnight." The man who came said, lying down on the left side of the opium couch.

This man was a little older than her, in his late thirties. A mediocre face of a high-ranking official showed a smile, and the white wool of the leather robe was exposed from the places that had never covered his calves. He had done a day of tedious and important things, and he brought a light heart like a kite. The kite was placed in the clouds, and Third Miss was the spring cloud surrounding this kite.

Chunyun poured tea for the kite, and grasped one of his hands with both hands, asking why he came late and made her wait for a long time.

"There are many things every day. These two days have been particularly busy. The store wants to check the goods, and I have to find things for others." The man said, bringing his mouth to Chunyun's lips. After a long time, Chunyun leaned against the other party.

"This day is going to exhaust people." Chunyun looked at his face with glittering eyes.

"I ran errands for Huang Xiaoliuzi in the morning, and I ran to him again until just now, and I finally got a clue."

"Is Huang Xiaoliuzi going to talk about something? That thing is extremely rogue."

"Last year, I arranged for him to work at Tongtai," his mouth held the mouth of the opium pipe that had been attached with a piece of opium, and his cheeks puffed up and down as he smoked. Immediately, two gray smoke came out of his nostrils first.

Chunyun interjected, "Didn't Tongtai close down?"

He nodded, and after finishing a mouthful, he groaned a sip of tea before continuing, "Yes, it's closed. Now I have to talk to someone else."

"Wasn't the business of the Tongtai family very good last year?"

"The people inside are all very good. But Shanghai was at war last year, and money couldn't circulate everywhere, so there was a financial turnover problem."

"The business on the street is still good. How could it lose money?"

"The business on the street is not good either. Business is getting worse every year. You naturally don't see it clearly on the outside."

"Then, think of a way, can't you close the store?"

The man laughed at these interesting words. He burned the opium in his hand and said, "Things aren't that easy there. Business is not good, and nothing can be turned around on the outside, so it's over. Recently, goods are expensive, and people in the countryside don't buy goods either."

"Why don't people in the countryside buy goods?" Chunyun looked at him again, happy in her heart.

"It's really strange, now everyone's business is smaller than before. Goods simply can't be sold."

"There are always a few that make money, right? Can they all be this bad?"

"Naturally there are some. Like the kerosene manager, the cigarette manager, the foreign sugar manager, as long as it's managing foreign goods, they always make money. But the daily foreign goods business is not necessarily making money. The years are getting worse year by year."

"I remember it didn't seem like I heard about it being so difficult to find a job a few years ago. It seems like it was more lively then than it is now. I don't know if it's because of luck? Or is it a calamity?"

Movie Supplement

Valuation of Major Hollywood Stars at the Beginning of the New Year (Middle)

— Xi Fu

Starting from the beginning of 1933

How prices rise and fall throughout the year

Only in his case, Wallace's little friend, Jackie Cooper, has fallen quite a bit. The fiery reputation he caused in the Skippy films has now waned a lot... Jackie is gradually growing up after all. But fortunately, since the release of "The Bowery", Jackie's market value, whether he is an adult or a child, has resurfaced with an upward trend. Jackie – he is a genius after all.

Joan Crawford, although she is undoubtedly a great actress, most of the critics who were consulted unanimously said that she has lost a lot of her brilliance in 1933, the reason being that she almost didn't get a script suitable for her status throughout the year. Fortunately, like Jackie Cooper, a new film, "Dancing Lady", came out, and the drop in her stock market value was immediately stopped.

Marion Davies and Ramon Novarro were able to maintain their original positions throughout the year. Although the stock market of the film industry is extremely turbulent, these two deeply respected stars have never fallen behind. Novarro has a deeply rooted influence in Spanish-speaking countries; that is his unique advantage, and he can rely on it for many more years without failing. In addition, Marie Dressler also maintained her baseline in the past year, but you need to know what kind of baseline her baseline is! She is the most beloved figure on the screen.

If we take the past year as a standard, then John Gilbert has become a thing of the past. But now he cannot be ignored again, because he has co-starred with the Swedish superstar Greta Garbo in Queen Christina. That film is said to be very successful. Therefore, his personal status can also be maintained from now on. As for Greta Garbo herself, that goes without saying. Anyone who leaves the screen for a year will definitely be eliminated, but Garbo? She is a mysterious woman, and the movie fans under her command are not just movie fans, they are simply crazy and follow her closely, never letting go!

Clark Gable's price in the stock market has dropped somewhat, but strangely, he is considered more valuable by the film company than before. 1933 was Gable's third year of widespread worship on the screen. The sensation when he first appeared on the screen has of course subsided a lot now, but he has released good films one after another, and he seems to have dug a very deep trench, which can make money for the company for many years without failing.

The one whose price dropped the most in the past year was Robert Montgomery. He needs divine help to restore his former glory; otherwise, he needs to release good films one after another, like "When Ladies Meet". Norma Shear has been away from the screen for too long, so her status has certainly been affected. Helen Hayes's price has neither risen nor fallen. Lee Tracy has improved a lot. But the most significant rise is Jean Harlow. She is quite likely to compete with Joan Crawford. If Joan doesn't take care of herself, her position will be taken by Jean. (To be continued)

A Third Party's Impartial Discussion on "The Good Earth"

— Shen Yu

Pearl S. Buck's "The Good Earth" caused quite a sensation in European and American literary circles and has also garnered much attention in China. Not long ago, someone wanted to adapt it into a screenplay, preparing to make a movie, but it did not succeed. Recently, there has been news that an American film company is sending people to China to film "The Good Earth." Consequently, Mr. Cao Yunxiang published an article in this publication explaining why "The Good Earth" should be filmed. This sparked a reaction from Mr. Luo Yang of Every Day Movie, to which Mr. Cao responded in a film special issue. Although I saw the previous two articles, I don't remember them clearly. Here, I want to take a third-party stance and say a few words based on "The Good Earth" novel and Mr. Cao's recent article.

According to Mr. Cao's writing, the first point of contention between Mr. Cao and Mr. Luo Yang is whether the protagonist Wang Lung's "feudal" consciousness should be portrayed.

Regarding this question, my opinion is as follows: In Chinese rural villages, feudal remnants are powerful. "Confucius's teachings" and "divine retribution" deeply envelop all farmers. Therefore, when using the Chinese countryside as a theme, depicting their feudal consciousness is inevitable and truthful. However, we must understand that because of the total collapse of the rural economy, this superstructure also wavers. Farmers, driven by hunger, bravely break through these "feudal" "remnants" and move forward. Only by breaking through these "feudal" "remnants" can there be a path to the future. Therefore, the most outstanding writers, in truly portraying the Chinese countryside, should first adopt a critical attitude when depicting "feudal remnants," indicating their gradual collapse. But is "The Good Earth" like this? Not at all. Pearl S. Buck is a religious believer; she simply praises these "feudal remnants." Needless to say, she is maintaining these "feudal remnants" rather than destroying them.

The second point is whether exposing the dark side of the Chinese countryside is malicious propaganda.

We believe that the idea of "not airing dirty linen in public" is incorrect. We should correctly expose all dark sides, especially the exploitation by local tyrants and landlords, the brutality of feudal warlords, and especially the aggression of imperialism. It is not enough to only depict superficial issues like opium and bandits. Therefore, we do not oppose "The Good Earth's" depiction of the dark side of the Chinese countryside, but we feel that what "The Good Earth" portrays is not the main evil. As for China's "natural disasters," in a word, they are all "man-made disasters." Before man-made disasters are alleviated, there is no way to avoid China's natural disasters. The dumping of foreign goods, the continuation of civil war, the heavy taxes, and the exploitation by local bullies are causing the farmers' last drop of blood to be drained. What strength do they have left to repair waterways and plant trees? Pearl S. Buck spent a lot of time in the Chinese countryside; couldn't she see these reasons? She saw them but deliberately didn't mention them. That is why Pearl S. Buck is Pearl S. Buck.

In short, "The Good Earth" is not a progressive novel. Although Pearl S. Buck's attitude is not like that of other "God's chosen people" who see the Chinese people as "semi-civilized" or "deserving of hardship," we see none of the heroic posture of Chinese farmers in "The Good Earth."

"Work hard, don't complain, God is the fairest." Perhaps Chinese farmers are the "children" in Pearl S. Buck's ideal? Unfortunately, they have become unruly.

Audience Opinions

After Watching "Twin Sisters"

— Jin Long

This is truly a miracle of the 1934 silver screen. The appropriate editing, perfect sound recording, and flexible direction all surpass Star Motion Picture Company's previous productions. Hu Die's success is even more unexpected to us. The acting is vivid and meticulous, and every line of dialogue touches the audience's heartstrings, exciting their emotions.

The director's use of techniques on the screen is also successful.

However, there seem to be some shortcomings in terms of makeup and set design, such as Zhao's mother appearing too old, which does not match her character's identity in the play, and the military law office for detaining prisoners being too luxurious.

The most satisfying aspect is the reduction of subtitles, with most of the plot conveyed through concise and moving dialogue, which is satisfactory.

The actors are all successful, and the most praiseworthy and successful, of course, is Hu Die. Her subtle expressions greatly enhance the film's achievements. Xuan Jinglin is also not bad. Tan Zhiyuan's performance in the later scenes is too contrived and over the top, which is typical of him.

In the barren Chinese film industry, the discovery of such a progressive work makes us believe that Mr. Zheng's directed films will not disappoint.

"The Return to Ordinariness"

— Lü Yi

"The Return" has broken the record for domestic films. That's correct. Why? Is it because its ideology is more correct than all other domestic films? No! Is it because the director surpasses all other domestic films? Also no! Are the actors or cinematography superior to all other domestic films? Still no! Then why do we say that "The Return" is setting a new record in the Chinese film industry? The answer is: because it used a foreign woman in a joint performance. It is wrong for us to praise and evaluate it simply because it used a foreign woman in a joint performance, because the merits of a film depend on the completeness of its content and form, and can never be determined by the actors' nationality.

Some people say that the good box office performance of "The Return" is entirely due to the appeal of Niki Tyna and a "kiss," which I think is not an exaggeration.

Rather than saying that "The Return" is a tragedy, it is better to say that "The Return" is a sound drama. No matter how painful and bitter the facts are, the ending is always happy.

The theme of "The Return," to put it in fashionable terms, is not necessarily realistic. Then, why did the author create this foreign love triangle story out of thin air? To deliberately show novelty? But "The Return" is far less flavorful than "Life." If "Life" is a cup of black tea, then "The Return" is like a glass of plain water. The plot of "Life" can stir people's emotions and give people lessons, but "The Return" only tells people an ordinary story. (To be continued)

Emil Jannings's "Merry Monarch" to be Released

The Shanghai branch of Universal Film Company has brought many excellent films to Shanghai audiences, such as "The Merry Widow," "Spring River Flows East," "Woman," "Forbidden Paradise," and "The Magician," which have all shocked the Chinese film industry and received excellent reviews. Now, they have another film, "Merry Monarch," to be screened at the Grand Shanghai Cinema.

This film is adapted from the famous work of the great French writer Pierre Louÿs, and the one left over is prepared for leap years. This story, on the surface, fully depicts the king's extravagant and sensual life, but in its essence, it opposes polygamy.

The world-renowned actor Emil Jannings plays the protagonist King Pusa in this film. The female lead is Shirley Vert, who is famous on the Hollywood film scene. The production cost of this film is nearly 18 million francs, most of which was shot in southern France, and a small part was set against the backdrop of ancient castles in Austria. Almost all the beauties of Paris were gathered, and it was also dubbed in both English and French. The copy with English dialogue will be screened at the Grand Shanghai Cinema. (Paid Advertisement)

"The Angry Tide of the China Sea" Performed

On the 28th in Beijing

"The Angry Tide of the China Sea," produced by Yi Hua Film Company, directed by Yue Feng, starring Yuan Meiyun, Cha Ruilong, Wang Yin, and Qin Tong, which has been completed after a considerable period of production, has been approved by the Nanjing Inspection Committee.

The theme of this film takes the fishing village as the background and promotes the national spirit as the main focus. The ideology is indeed commendable, and the actors' expressions, the director's techniques, and the camera work and editing have all achieved great success. It has been determined that this film will be performed at the Beijing Grand Theater on the 28th of this month.

Film Novel

Queen Christina XVI

— Hu Chen

The next morning, Christina sat on the throne, with ministers and representatives of the people standing below. She stood up and announced her will to the public. Everyone listened, looked at each other in surprise, and then burst into a loud chorus of "No, no!" It turned out that what the queen announced was that she had decided to abdicate in favor of Prince Charles. Prime Minister Oxenstierna cried out in exasperation, "Your Majesty, you can't!" Christina raised her hand to first stop the uproar, and then said to the Prime Minister, "Oxenstierna, please take my crown off." Oxenstierna shouted, "I can't. I swore before your late father that I would always keep the crown on your head. I can't participate in this. I don't think any of the ministers in court dare to do this." Christina slowly said, "Then I can only take it off myself." After she finished speaking, she silently placed the scepter she held in her hand on the case in front of her, then raised her hand to take off the crown herself and placed it next to the scepter. She then untied the belt of her robe, letting it fall, revealing a white dress inside. She stood in front of the crowd and gave them her farewell. She said, "You don't need to be afraid for me. I am at peace. From now on, I will no longer be ruled by fate. No matter what I encounter, I will always be happy. God bless you. Goodbye. Above me, only God has authority." After she finished speaking, she walked step by step, without looking back, towards the palace gate.

In the port of Danzig, there was a ship moored there, already rigged and ready to sail. Christina took a few attendants and walked there. The captain rushed forward and bowed, saying, "Although Your Majesty has given up your throne, Your Majesty is still Your Majesty." Christina quickly asked, "Where is Antonio?" The captain said, "Your Majesty, he's on the ship," but the sadness in his voice made her heart feel a pang of sorrow. She quickly walked onto the ship from the gangplank, looking for Antonio on the deck. A person ran over from the front, but it was not Antonio, but Magnus. Their eyes met. Christina asked, "Where is Antonio?" She felt another pang of sorrow, because her eyes had already caught sight of something that looked like a coffin, covered with silk cloth. Magnus pointed to the thing and said, "He's inside." Christina said, "He's |in| there." She was flustered, like a prisoner awaiting judgment.

Magnus took a step forward and shouted, "That was a fair duel, and he insisted on it. It was either him or me. I won... though it was an unfortunate victory, because you would have spared me." Christina said, "Magnus, you leave this ship." Magnus said bitterly, "I'm glad I beat him. I knew he and I were irreconcilable." Christina urged again, "Magnus, you leave this ship." Magnus walked away. She immediately knelt beside the coffin and shouted, "Antonio!" She uncovered the silk cloth covering the corpse, silently grieved for a while, then covered it again, sobbing, "Antonio! Antonio! Antonio, whom I call a hundred times and he doesn't respond! Antonio, to whom I have declared my love a thousand times! I'll say it again now, I love you... I love you... forever and ever..." She stood up and called her old servant Olaf, telling him to order the captain to set sail immediately. Olaf said with tears streaming down his face, "Won't Your Majesty wait a moment longer?" Christina said, "No waiting, tell him to set sail." She stood beside the coffin, facing the boundless sea. The ship slowly sailed out, towards where the sun sets. (The End)
